{Welcome to The IBM HandShaker.:Color_1}

This integrated environment is designed for software development.
providing controllers and communication with them via COM ports.

By selecting any menu item and pressing the F1 key, you can call up the Help window,
which contains information about what this item is for and how
use it.

item ------------------------------------------------------------is called by pressing Alt+Spacebar. All other items
are called by pressing Alt+Z, where Z is the first letter of the menu item. Call
You can also select an item by pointing to it with the mouse cursor and pressing the left button.

To call up {a list of all menu items:Contents}, press Shift+F1.

To remove the Help window from the screen, press Esc.

.topic Dragging
You can move the window around using the keyboard arrows or the mouse.
screen. In addition, you can resize windows by clicking
Shift + arrow keys or by clicking the mouse cursor on the lower right corner
windows and moving the mouse.

Once you've selected the desired position, press Enter. Cancel - Esc.

When executing this command from the menu, hold down the Ctrl key

.topic SEnvDlg
{ ------------------------------------------------------------ｳEnvironment (Alt+F11) :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ

.topic EnvDlg
{ Environment editor :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Environment Editor dialog box contains:

  list variables environment variables
  line editing (Edit)
  Modify, New, Delete, Copy, Done buttons

The Modify command makes the edit line with the selected line active.
environment variable.

The New command adds an empty string to the variable list,
after which it executes the Modify command.

The Delete command removes the selected environment variable from the list.

The Copy command copies the contents of the list to the {Clipboard}.

The Done command closes the dialog box and refreshes the list of variables.
environment in the program memory.

It is possible to reserve a place in the environment using
a special variable named $CNSAVE and a value equal to any
a line starting with the '#' character (ASCII 35), for example:

$CNSAVE=##################################

Upon detecting such a variable, the environment editor will automatically
shorten its length when adding other variables and expand
while reducing other variables.

.topic ASCIITable
{ ASCII Table :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The ASCII table contains the complete character set of the IBM PC. The current character
highlighted by the cursor. You can use the keyboard or
"mouse". If the table is open above the editor window, then when you press the key
Enter or double-click the mouse button to insert the current character.
to the cursor position; if the Ctrl key was pressed, the table window
will close. Right-click or press Ctrl+Down, Ctrl+Up
The {Key codes:KeyView} dialog box is called up, showing the expanded
scan code of the pressed key or key combination, for example, Alt+Back ($0100).

.topic SCalculator
{ ------------------------------------------------------------ｳCalculator (Alt+L) :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Calculator command displays the programmer's calculator on the screen.
({Calculator}).

.topic Calculator
{ Calculator :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
This is a multifunctional calculator that works in hexadecimal,
decimal, octal, and binary number systems. Work with it
You can do this using the keyboard or by clicking the calculator buttons with the mouse.

The 'R' button resets; the '' button (BackSpace key) erases the last
the entered character; the buttons '!', '&', '|', '^' perform the corresponding actions
logical functions (NOT, AND, OR, XOR); the '_' button assigns a value
minus sign; the '' button ('Ctrl+R') performs the calculation of the reciprocal value;
The 'S' and 'Q' buttons perform squaring and square root calculations
respectively.

To switch between displays, use the Tab key or your mouse.
To switch from one {mode:ToggleHex} to another on the lower display
Use Down, Up keys or mouse (double click).
To move from one {range:ToggleCalc} to another, use
Left, Right keys.

The arrows to the left and right of the top display serve respectively to
{write to memory:CalcPush} and {retrieve from memory:CalcPop}. For
to perform these operations, click the corresponding arrow with the mouse or
Press Ctrl+, Ctrl+.

.topic ToggleHex
Setting the calculator's lower display mode (Hex, Octal, Binary).

.topic ToggleCalc
Setting the calculator's operating range (Range):

  Real (-1.7E38..1.7E38)
  Shortint (-128..127)
  Integer (-32768..32767)
  Longint (-2147483648..2147483647)
  Byte (0..255)
  Word (0..65535)

.topic CalcPush
The Push to memory command (Ctrl+Up) writes the number on the top key to memory.
calculator display. You can retrieve numbers from memory with the command
{Pop from memory:CalcPop}.

.topic CalcPop
The Pop from memory command (Ctrl+Down) opens a window with numbers,
written to memory by the command {Push to memory:CalcPush}. Selected
The number will appear on the calculator's top display.

.topic Expressions
The Expressions command (Ctrl+Enter) opens a dialog box.
{Solve expressions:SolveExprDlg}.

.topic SolveExprDlg
{ Solve expressions :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Solve expressions dialog box is designed for calculating
{mathematical expressions:CtrlQM}.

The window consists of a line for entering expressions and a panel on which
The calculation result is displayed in various formats. Result
calculations are shown on the panel immediately during the change process
contents of the line. If the line for entering expressions contains partial text
selected (Shift+Right, Shift+Left), the calculation is performed only for
the selected part of the expression. The panel also contains switches
Copy as to select the format of the result when copying
in {Clipboard} using the Copy command.

The Evaluate (Enter) command is used to substitute the resulting
the calculation result (in decimal format) into the input line
expressions.

You can enter expressions containing variables sequentially,
For example:

A5 := 14.78
B := 23.91
LN(2) * (A5 + SQRT(B))

Result = 13.6340562039

In order to execute the menu command {Calculator:SCalculator}
(Alt+L, Ctrl+Alt+L) always opened a dialog box
Solve expressions instead of the usual {calculator:Calculator}, you need
Enable the Always open this dialog box rather than Calculator window checkbox.

.topic SAlarm
{ ------------------------------------------------------------ｳAlarm (Alt+<) :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Alarm clock command displays the {Alarm list:Alarm} dialog box.

.topic Alarm
{ Alarm list :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Alarm list dialog box contains:

  list items?
  Modify, New, Delete, Adjust buttons

The Modify command brings up the {Modify item:NewItem} dialog box,
in which you can change the parameters of a previously entered item.

The New command displays the {New item:NewItem} dialog box,
which allows you to include a new item in the Items list.

The Delete command removes an item from the Items list.

The {Adjust:NewItemPos} command allows you to move an item to a different location.
on the list.

.topic NewItem
{ New item / Modify item :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
In the New item / Modify item dialog box, the date and time are set,
about the occurrence of which you want to be warned, as well as
warning text. At the specified moment, a sound will be heard
signal and a window with warning text will appear.

If the date is not specified or is specified incorrectly, the program sets
current date; if time is not specified, the program sets 0 (zero).

If the Everyday option is enabled, the item will be executed daily.

If the Execute if overdue option is enabled, the item will be executed,
if the time has expired (the program was not running at that time).

If the Delete after execution option is enabled, the item will be deleted.
after execution.

.topic SSpooler
{ ------------------------------------------------------------ｳSpooler (Alt+>) :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Spooler command displays the {Spooler} dialog box.

.topic Spooler
{ Spooler :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Spooler dialog box contains:

  list windows or files V queues printer (Spooler queue)
  File, Next, Delete, Abort buttons

The File command allows you to use the {file dialog:FileDialog}
select and place a file on disk into the printer queue (see also
directive {$PRINT:Directives}).

The Next command puts the selected window or file first in the queue after
currently being printed.

The Delete command removes a window or file from the printer queue.

The Abort command clears the queue and reinitializes the printer.

.topic SDialer
{ ------------------------------------------------------------ｳDialer (Alt+?) :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Dialer command displays the {Dialer} dialog box.

.topic Dialer
{ Dialer :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Dialer dialog box contains:

  list telephone numbers V queues
autodialer
  buttons Redial, Abort, Insert, Load,
Paste, Delete, Adjust

In each line of the list, in addition to the phone number itself, there may be
there must be a comment separated by the ';' symbol, for example:

214-35-76; Ivan Petrovich

The Redial command starts auto-dialing from the number on which the cursor is located.
If the Ctrl key is pressed, the dialog box closes.

The program calls each number on the list in turn with a delay,
specified in the {Modem setup:ModemSetup} dialog box until
until the CD (Carrier Detect) signal appears or until the operation is
interrupted by the Abort command (Esc key in the {Terminal} window).

The list can be filled with Insert commands (entering the number manually),
Load (load from a text file selected using
{file dialog:FileDialog}), Paste (from the {Clipboard} window),
and also from the {Terminal} and {Phone list:PhoneBook} windows using the Dial command.

The Delete command removes the current number from the queue. If you press
Ctrl key clears the entire list.

The {Adjust:NewItemPos} command allows you to move a number to a different location.
on the list.

{ ------------------------------------------------------------ｳCD Player (Ctrl+F11) :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ

{ ｺ :AbsColor_$3F} {:AbsColor_$3E} {Stairway To Heaven:AbsColor_$3F} ﾛﾛﾛｲｲｲｲｲｲｲｲｲｲｲｲｲｲｲｲｲｲ ｲｲｲｲｲｲｲｲｲｲｲｲｲｲｲｲｲｲｲｲｲ { ｺ :AbsColor_$3F}
{ ﾈﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｼ :AbsColor_$3F}

The window contains a display for showing the track number and the current time.
playback, an information line showing the status of the CD-ROM drive
or the name of the composition being played, a "slider" displaying the process
playback, as well as the following buttons:

[  ] Stop
[ ﾍ ] Play
[ || ] Pause
[ ] Eject
[ [ ] Skip back
[ ] Rewind
[ ] Fast forward
[ ] ] Skip forward

[ Track ] Select track
[ Album ] Album file
[ Lyrics ] Album lyrics
[ Mix ] Sound Mixer
[ Options ] CD Player options

CD Player window commands:

Ctrl+S, S Stop
Ctrl+P, P Play
Ctrl+U, U Pause
Ctrl+J, J Eject
Ctrl+I, I Skip back
Ctrl+R, R Rewind
Ctrl+F, F Fast forward
Ctrl+N, N Skip forward

Ctrl+T Toggle display track mode
Ctrl+D Toggle display time mode
Ctrl+W Tracklist

Right Fast Forward
Left Rewind
Ctrl+Right Skip forward
Ctrl+Left Skip back
Ins,
Ctrl+Ins Eject
Home Begin track
End Skip Forward
Ctrl+Home First track
Ctrl+End Last track

After inserting the CD, the following appears at the top of the display frame:
switches for displaying the number and duration of a composition:

Track Current track number
Total number of tracks on the disc

Track time The current playing time of the composition
Track total Total playing time of the current track
Track left Time remaining until the end of the current track
Disk time Current playing time of the CD
Disk total Total playing time of a compact disc
Disk left Time left on the CD

These modes are switched by pressing the mouse button or the keys Ctrl+T and
Ctrl+D. If you hold down the Shift key, the time display mode
switches in the opposite direction.

Clicking the mouse button in the area where the number or number of tracks is displayed
on the display causes the Select track command to be executed.

The Stop command stops playback and moves the reading head.
to the beginning of the CD. If you hold down the Ctrl key, it will execute
reinitializing the CD-ROM drive.

The Play command starts playback.

The Pause command pauses or restarts playback.

The Eject command moves the CD-ROM drive door out or in. If you hold down
the Ctrl key, the command will be executed even if the door is locked
(see also {OptionsｳCD Player:OCDOptions}).

The Skip back command rewinds to the beginning of the previous track.

The Rewind command performs fast rewind.

The Fast forward command performs fast forward.

The Skip forward command skips to the beginning of the next track.

The Begin track command rewinds to the beginning of the current track.

The First track command rewinds to the beginning of the first track.

The Last track command rewinds to the beginning of the last track.

The Select track command opens a dialog box.
{Select a track to play:CDTracks}, which allows you to select a track number
for playback.

The Track list command (Ctrl+W) opens a window
{Track list window:CDTrackList}.

The Album command opens a file in the {text editor:ASCIIEditor} window,
containing the album title and the list of tracks on the CD
(See also {CD albums:CDAlbums}). If in the CD albums directory
(see also {OptionsｳCD Player:OCDOptions}) there is no such file, it is created and
filled with composition numbers.

The album title is displayed in the frame of the CD Player window, the title of the current
compositions - in the information line under the buttons.

The Lyrics command is used to view the lyrics of the songs on an album.
(see also {CD albums:CDAlbums}).

The Mix command starts the Sound Mixer program specified in the line
Sound Mixer command dialog box {CD Player options:OCDOptions},
which can be called by the Options command.

.topic CDTracks
The Select a track to play dialog box allows you to choose which track to play.
any composition from the CD. The window contains buttons
with the numbers of all the compositions that become active when pressed
corresponding number keys, for example 04 or 12.

.topic CDTrackList
The Track list window contains a list of the titles of all the tracks specified.
in the {CD album:CDAlbums} file corresponding to the given compact disc.
{CD Player:CDPlayer} starts playback from the selected
compositions.

.topic CDAlbums
For any CD, use the Album command of the {CD Player:CDPlayer} window
you can create a text file with a name that matches the unique
characteristics of this disc, and the .CD extension, consisting of the following
lines:

TITLE: Album title; Total running time
$LYRICS: Command for viewing song lyrics
01: Title of the first composition; Playing time
02: Title of the second composition; Playing time
* * * * * *
12: Title of the last composition; Playing time

The file is created in the CD albums directory.
(see also {OptionsｳCD Player:OCDOptions}).

The {$LYRICS:Color_2} directive is used to view the lyrics of an album.
when running the Lyrics command. Examples of its use:

$LYRICS:$HELP($CN\CD\LYRICS.HLP) [Search string]

or

$LYRICS:$VIEW(D:\MUSIC\LYRICS\LYRICS.TXT)

The first example opens the Help window with the LYRICS.HLP file from the subdirectory
CD in the program's working directory and search for the Search string
or, if not specified, the title of the current composition among those listed
in the first context of the points.
The second example opens the {Text viewer:TextViewer} window for viewing
file LYRICS.TXT, located in the D:\MUSIC\LYRICS directory.

{$LYRICS:Color_2} command line directives can also be found
after the title of each composition. In this case, for each composition there will be
execute your own text viewing command, for example:

01:Title of the first composition $LYRICS:$VIEW(TRACK01.TXT)
02:Title of the second composition $LYRICS:$VIEW(TRACK02.TXT)
* * * * * *
12:Title of the last song $LYRICS:$VIEW(TRACK12.TXT)

If the text view command is executed for any composition
should not (for example, the composition is purely instrumental), it is necessary to use
directive {$NOLYRICS:Color_2}:

* * * * * *
04:The title of the fourth composition is $NOLYRICS
* * * * * *

To automatically execute the Lyrics command each time you play
the composition is served by the directive {$AUTO:Color_2}, which must be located
at the end of the main line with the {$LYRICS:Color_2} directive:

$LYRICS:$HELP($CN\CD\LYRICS.HLP) $AUTO

The order of numbers and titles of compositions is used when
playback in User order mode, while the track numbers can
repeat.

.topic ASCIIEditor,AltASCIIEditor
{Edit window :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The file editor window contains the contents of the selected file.
in ASCII format. You can navigate the file using the mouse or
keyboards:

Up Move up one line
Down Go down a line
Right Shift one character to the right
Left Shift one character to the left
PgUp Go up one page
PgDn Scroll down one page
Home Return to first column
End Move to the last column
Ctrl+PgUp Return to the beginning of the file
Ctrl+PgDn Move to the end of the file
Ctrl+Left Move one word to the left
Ctrl+Right Move one word to the right
Ctrl+Home Move to the top line
Ctrl+End Move to the bottom line

The indicator in the lower left corner of the window shows the current position of the cursor,
the decimal value of the character the cursor is on, as well as the mode
block selection: solid [] or vertical [].
The '*' symbol means that the file in the window has been modified.

You can move the window, resize it, and close it using
{Window} menu item commands.

The text editor window menu is called by right-clicking
or by pressing Alt+F10.

ASCII editor commands:

Backspace Delete the character before the cursor
Delete Deletes the character at the cursor position.
Enter Go to the next line
Ins Toggle Insert/Overwrite mode
Alt+K Toggle block selection mode
Alt+Y Select an existing marker using the {Place markers:PlaceMarkerDlg} window
Ctrl+A Select all command (select all text)
Ctrl+B Command {Search again:SHSearchAgain} (repeat search for a string, Backward)
Ctrl+L Command {Search again:SHSearchAgain} (search for a string again)
Ctrl+T Delete word to the right
Ctrl+U Command {Search again:SHSearchAgain} (repeat search for a string, Forward)
Ctrl+Back Delete the word to the left
Ctrl+Y Delete line
Ctrl+@ Incremental search mode ({Incremental search:EditIncSearch})
Ctrl+Space Selects the word at the cursor position for the {Search again:SHSearchAgain} command
Ctrl+- Duplicate line
Ctrl+^ Duplicate the character above the cursor
Ctrl+] Swap words to the left and right of the cursor
Ctrl+\ Go to the {File Manager:Panel} window and search for the current file

Shift+F2 Counts the number of words and characters in the selected block or in the entire text
Shift+F4 Spell Check starting from the word under the cursor (Spell Check)
Shift+F8 Deletes the word under the cursor from the Spell Checker dictionary

See also

{Ctrl+K commands:CtrlKPressed}
{Ctrl+Q commands:CtrlQPressed}
{Ctrl+P commands:CtrlPPressed}
{Ctrl+O commands:CtrlOPressed}
{Block Drag-And-Drop:BlockDragAndDrop}

.topic CtrlPPressed
Some symbols, for example, 
(Ctrl+K), 
(Ctrl+L), (Ctrl+Y), etc.,
are the controls for the editor window. To enter such a symbol in
To edit text from the keyboard, you must first press Ctrl+P.
Using {ASCII table:ASCIITable} you can enter any character into the text.

.topic CtrlOPressed
Pressing Ctrl+O n, where n is one of the following characters,
toggles the corresponding {local editor options:EditOptions}:

'C' - Create backup files;
'I' - Insert mode;
'A' - Autoindent mode;
'U' - Use tab characters;
'X' - Use expanded memory;
'P' - Prompt on new file;
'H' - Change dir on open;
'N' - Cascade new window;
'F' - Find text at cursor;
'D' - Enable Undo/Redo;
'R' - Enable text wrap;
'B' - Enable hyphenation;
'L' - Expand wrapped line;
'S' - Syntax highlight;
'G' - Highlight current line;
'O' - Highlight current column;
'T' - Highlight page breaks;
'<',
'>' - Highlight boundaries;
'-',
'_' - Non-persistent blocks;
'V' - Overwrite blocks;
' ' - Keep trailing blanks;
']' - Wrap lines on Load;
'[' - Unwrap lines on Save;
'Y' - Literal key input;
Tab - Enable smart tab cursor movement;
'(' - Add matching chars;
',',
'.',
':',
';',
'!',
'?' - Auto-spaces after stops;
'E' - Esc closes;
'Q' - opens the {Editor options:EditOptions} dialog box
to set local editor options.

See also {Editor group list:CommentDlg}

.topic DrawSingle,DrawDouble
To draw lines, move the cursor with the arrows while pressing the Shift key.
To cancel drawing mode, press Esc.

approximate position in the file (%), as well as the block selection mode:
solid [] or vertical [].

You can move the window, resize it, and close it using
{Window} menu item commands.

Text viewer window commands:

Alt+K Toggle block selection mode
Alt+Y Select an existing marker using the {Place markers:PlaceMarkerDlg} window
Ctrl+A Select all command (select all text)
Ctrl+B Command {Search again:SHSearchAgain} (repeat search for a string, Backward)
Ctrl+L Command {Search again:SHSearchAgain} (search for a string again)
Ctrl+U Command {Search again:SHSearchAgain} (repeat search for a string, Forward)
Ctrl+@ Incremental search mode ({Incremental search:EditIncSearch})
Space Selects the word at the cursor position for the {Search again:SHSearchAgain} command
Ctrl+\ Go to the {File Manager:Panel} window and search for the current file

You can switch from viewing to editing using the command
{Reload as ASCII (Alt+A):WUpdateASCII}.

Pressing Ctrl+QA opens another Text viewer window c
the file being viewed.

See also

{Ctrl+K commands:ViewerCtrlKPressed}
{Ctrl+Q commands:ViewerCtrlQPressed}

.topic HexViewer,AltHexViewer
{ Hex view window :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The binary file viewer window displays the contents of the selected file.
in Hex format. You can navigate through the file using the mouse or
keyboards:

Up Move up one line
Down Go down a line
Right Shift one character to the right
Left Shift one character to the left
PgUp Go up one page
PgDn Scroll down one page
Home Return to first column
End Move to the last column
Ctrl+PgUp Return to the beginning of the file
Ctrl+PgDn Move to the end of the file
Ctrl+Left Move one word to the left
Ctrl+Right Move one word to the right
Ctrl+Home Move to the top line
Ctrl+End Move to the bottom line

You can move the window, resize it, and close it using
{Window} menu item commands.

Hex viewer window commands:

Alt+Y Select an existing marker using the {Place markers:PlaceMarkerDlg} window
Ctrl+A Select all command (select all text)

Ctrl+\ Go to the {File Manager:Panel} window and search for the current file

Hex viewer allows you to edit the contents of the file being viewed.
only in Overwrite mode, in which case the changed characters are highlighted.

buffer the next portion of the file (for example, when scrolling), a prompt will appear:

 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Confirm ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ
 ｺ                                      ｺ
 ｺ Save changes to disk ｺ
 ｺ before loading another portion of ｺ
 ｺ D:\CONNECT\SOMEFILE.EXE ? ｺ

 ｺ { Yes :AbsColor_$5f} ﾜ { No :AbsColor_$50} ﾜ        ｺ
 ｺ          ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ    ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ        ｺ
 ﾈﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｼ

.topic CtrlQI
Logical or arithmetic operation for all characters in the selected block:

Char and Mask
Char OR Mask
Char XOR Mask
Char + Mask
Char - Mask

The Mask string can be a sequence of hexadecimal digits.
or ASCII characters (if it starts with the character ' (ASCII 39)),
For example:

0B 1F 3D 15 81 6C
$0B, $1F, $3D, $15, $81, $6C
Some password

.topic CtrlQJ
Formatting the current paragraph from the cursor position.

.topic CtrlQK
Find the end of the selected block.

.topic CtrlQL
Convert all characters in the selected block or current line to lowercase.

.topic CtrlQM
The Math operation command produces the operation specified in the dialog box.
mathematical operation on all numbers in the selected block
(or the current line) and places the result at the cursor position.

If the Formula mode is selected, the program calculates the value of the expression,
which may include the following functions and operators:

ARCCOS, ARCSIN, ARCTG - Result in radians
SING - Sine of an angle in degrees
SIN - Sine of an angle in radians
COSG - Cosine of an angle in degrees
COS - Cosine of an angle in radians
CTGG - Cotangent of an angle in degrees
CTG - Cotangent of an angle in radians
TGG - Tangent of an angle in degrees
TG - Tangent of an angle in radians
SQRT - Square Root
LG - Common logarithm
LN - Natural logarithm
EXP10 - 10 to the power
EXP - Exponent
ABS - Absolute Value

"+", "-", "*", "/" - main
arithmetic operations;

"^" - raising to a power (2^8);

"%" - integer division;

"&&", "||", "#", "<<", ">>", Not() - bitwise operations
"AND", "OR", "XOR", "SHL", "SHR", Not.

Hexadecimal numbers are entered with the $, 0x prefix, or the H postfix.
$1000, 0x1000, 1000h = 4096
Binary numbers are entered with the prefix 0b or the postfix B.
0b1000, 1000b = 8
Octal numbers are entered with the prefix 0o or the postfix O.
0o1000, 1000o = 512
You can enter numbers in the format \377 = 255, \e = 27, \n = 10.

Input of numbers in a special engineering format is supported:

1T = 1E12 (tera)
1G = 1E9 (giga)
1M = 1E6 (mega)
1k = 1K = 1E3 (kilo)
1d = 1D = 1E1 (decimals)
1s = 1E-2 (centi)
1m = 1E-3 (milli)
1u = 1E-6 (micro)
1n = 1E-9 (nano)
1p = 1E-12 (peak)
1f = 1E-15 (femto)
1f = 1E-18 (atto)

The constant Pi = 3.1415926535 is defined

Any level of nesting of parentheses is allowed.

The length of the formula must not exceed 255 characters (excluding spaces).

Program mode allows you to evaluate expressions containing variables,
For example:

A5 := 14.78
B := 23.91
LN(2) * (A5 + SQRT(B))

Result = 13.6340562039

Each statement in a program must begin on a new line, unlike
from the "Formula" mode, which allows the wrapping of long lines, subject to
conditions for a maximum length of 255 characters, for example:

LN(2) * (14.78 +
SQRT(23.91))

Variables can have arbitrary names consisting of the following
characters: 0 .. 9, _, $, A .. Z, a .. z, case does not matter.

.topic CtrlQNew
The Open file at cursor command opens a new editor window for
file with the name pointed to by the cursor in the current window.

.topic CtrlQPath
The Make directory at cursor command creates a new directory with the name,
which the cursor points to in the current window (if such a directory already exists,
nothing happens).

.topic CtrlQO
The Unformat text command allows you to remove extra spaces from the selected text.
between words, leaving only one.

.topic CtrlQPrint
Print screen output.

.topic CtrlQR
The Reformat text command allows you to reformat the selected text in
depending on the options set in the Reformat dialog box
formatting options:

  Line width - width lines
  Left margin - indent left
(when wrapping lines)

  Global - all text
  Selected text - marked block

If the Paragraphs option is enabled, then when formatting text, the following will be used:
paragraphs (lines with an indentation greater than the Left margin) must be respected,
will not be transferred).

If the Word hyphenation option is enabled, the program will, if necessary,
transfer words according to her ideas about how it is done.

If the Expand lines option is enabled, the program will expand the lines if necessary.
expand the transferred line with spaces to the length of Line width.

.topic CtrlQS
Line drawing mode:DrawSingle (Single).

.topic CtrlQT
The Date/Time stamp command inserts the current date and time at the cursor position.
in the format determined by the {Country settings:OCountry} dialog settings,
For example:

March 19, 1996, 08:35:54

Pressing Ctrl+Q will insert only the date,
and when you press the keys Ctrl+Q | - only time.

.topic CtrlQU
Convert all characters in the selected block or current line to uppercase.

.topic CtrlQV
{Ctrl+QV:Color_2} - translate the selected block or the current line into Volapyuk
(Moldovianizer:).

{Ctrl+Q ,:Color_2} - reverse translation.

.topic CtrlQW
Translate all characters in the selected block or the current line using
table for conversion stored in the CONNECT.TBL file (if the following were pressed)
keys Ctrl+Q+Q, then the {file dialog:FileDialog} opens to select a file).
The table is a 256-byte character array.

.topic CtrlQX
Sorting lines in a selected block alphabetically
(ascending or descending). The Case sensitive flag indicates that
It is necessary to distinguish between uppercase and lowercase letters. If the position in the line is specified,
string comparison is performed from this position.

.topic CtrlQY
Delete from the cursor position to the end of the line.

.topic CtrlQZ
Delete from the cursor position to the end of the file.

.topic CtrlQCaps
Translate the first letters of all words in the selected block or current line
to uppercase (Capitalize).

.topic CtrlQSpace
Remove blank lines from a selected block or from the entire file.

.topic OtherCtrlQ
Various text formatting commands.

.topic SetTextMode
The Set UNIX/DOS text mode command sets the corresponding mode
editor's work with text files.

.topic EditIncSearch
Sequential text search mode by letters from the cursor position
(Incremental search).

Press the keys corresponding to the letters of the word you are looking for in sequence.
To find the next word that contains a substring that has already been found,
Press Ctrl+L, to find the previous one - Ctrl+B. To go back one step
Back press the Backspace key. To exit sequential mode
To search, press the Esc key or any cursor movement key.

See also {SearchｳFind:SHFind}.

.topic BlockDragAndDrop
{ Block Drag-And-Drop :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
You need to "take" the selected block with the mouse by pressing both of its buttons
(left and right, with the left first; to perform the Move block
press the Ctrl or Alt key). A moving window will appear on the screen.
along with the mouse. After that, one of the buttons, as well as the Ctrl (Alt) key
You can release it. If you place the window over this or another editor window
(ASCII or Hex) and release it, the Copy block operation will be performed or
Move block, and if in any other place - Delete block operation. To cancel
Press Esc.

.topic Snipper
{ Snipper :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
Snipper is a resident program that allows you to edit text in text mode.
display transfer screen contents to {Clipboard}. Program
initialized by pressing Alt+Ctrl+W, while on the screen
a cursor appears. The beginning and end of the block selection is performed
press the Enter key, select using the control keys, and cancel using the Esc key.
The memorization operation can be performed until it overflows.
buffer, as indicated by a beep. To download Snipper
must be specified in the command line of the launching program CN.EXE
the following parameters:

[/Bxxxx]/S
xxxx - buffer size, bytes
( 2048 Bytes by default )

Example: CN/S or CN/B8192/S

Another way to load Snipper is to run another program with the command
{Execute:UExecute} with the Load Snipper flag and Unload option enabled.

.topic ECopyToAddClip
{ EditｳCopy to additional Clipboard (Ctrl+F12) :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ

into the temporary file CONNECT.CLP, located in the directory specified

See also {EditｳPaste from additional Clipboard:EPasteFromAddClip}

.topic ESaveClipData
{ EditｳSave Clipboard data on exit :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Save Clipboard data on exit command toggles the mode in which
The contents of the {Clipboard} window are saved to disk when you exit
programs and can be used the next time they are launched.

{ATTENTION!!!:Color_4}
When the Clipboard content preservation mode is enabled, the data on
disk will constantly accumulate. To prevent this situation,
at which the data no longer fits into the program memory,
It is necessary to periodically delete files before launching
CNxxxxxx.@@@ and CNxxxxxx.###, located in the directory specified in
the Setup dialog box ({OptionsｳSetupｳSwap file directory:Setup}),
or turn off this mode from time to time.

.topic EFillHex
{ Fill :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Fill command allows you to fill any area of the editable area.
in the Hex file format with any character. The command calls
the Fill Hex dialog box where you specify the fill area
and the symbol used by the program to fill the given area.
The area is specified by a start and end address, for example, 001FA:007ED,
and the symbol - its ordinal Hex number or directly as a letter or
a number preceded by the symbol ', for example, 7B or 'Q.

.topic RegExp
{ Regular expression :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The program can recognize specifiers similar to those used
in the GREP program, in the search line.
The specifiers are ^, $, ., *, +, [], \. They mean the following:

^ - at the beginning of a line means the beginning of a line.
$ - at the end of an expression means the end of a line.
. - means any symbol.
* - a symbol followed by an asterisk,
means any number
repetitions (including zero) of this
symbol. For example, bo* means bot, b,
boo, and even be.
+ - a symbol followed by a plus sign,
means any number of repetitions of this
character (but not zero). For example, bo+
means bot or boo, but not be or b.
? - a symbol followed by a question mark
means one or no characters.
[] - symbols in square brackets mean
any one symbol standing in these
brackets. For example, [bot] means either b,
either o or t.
[^] - this sign in square brackets at the beginning
lines means "not". Thus,
[^bot] means any character except
b, o or t.
[-] - inside square brackets means
range of characters. For example, [bo]
means any character from b to o.
\ - before the specifier symbol says
to the editor about what is needed
consider this symbol as a letter,
and not as a specifier. For example, \^
means ^, not the beginning of a line.
(r) - means r and represents a group.
| - between symbols or expressions in
round brackets means logical
OR between these expressions.

See also {Replace}

.topic UnixWildcard
{ UNIX style wildcards :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
UNIX style mask is a special type
{regular expression:RegExp}. '*' matches any number of
any characters; '?' matches any character; characters enclosed
in '[]' matches any of the characters listed in brackets.
It is also possible to specify a range in the form [a-z]. The '^' symbol after the '['
means any character except those listed in brackets. To cancel this
the action of the symbol '^' is escaped with the symbol '\'. Thus, the expression
of the form '[\^~]' matches the character '^' or the character '~'.

.topic SHFind
{ SearchｳFind :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Find command allows you to find the file you need in the editor window.
ASCII or Hex string.

See also {Find}

.topic Find
{ Find :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
Enter the search string (in the {Hex Editor:HexEditor} windows,
{Hex Viewer:HexViewer} and {Dump:Mem} you can use the $ symbol
at the beginning of the string if this string is a number in Hex format).
When the Case sensitive option is enabled, the program distinguishes between large
and lowercase letters. If the From cursor option is enabled, the search is performed
from the cursor position, otherwise - from the beginning of the file. If enabled
The Whole words only option searches for whole words only. If enabled
Regular expression option, the program can recognize specifiers,
similar to those used in the GREP program, in the search line
(see also {Regular expression:RegExp}). If the option is enabled
Selected text, the search is carried out only in the selected area.
If the Search backward option is enabled, the search is performed in the reverse direction.

.topic SHReplace
{ SearchｳReplace :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Replace command allows you to find the text you need in the edited text.
line and replace it with another.

See also {Replace}

.topic Replace
{ Replace :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
Enter the search string and the replace string. When this option is enabled
Case sensitive program distinguishes between upper and lower case letters.
If the From cursor option is enabled, the search is performed from the cursor position,
otherwise, from the beginning of the file. If the Whole words only option is enabled,
Only whole words are searched. If the Regular expression option is enabled,
the program can recognize specifiers similar to those used in
GREP program, in the search line (see also {Regular expression:RegExp}).
When the Regular expression option is enabled, the replacement string may contain
the following control characters:

& - Inserts the original string.
\n - Inserts the text matched by group number 'n' (0-9).

For example, searching for an expression

{([AZ]+)([0-9]+):Color_2}

in a line

{--- AB56 ---:Color_2}

and replacing it with

{& -> \1\0:Color_2}

will result in

{---AB56 -> 56AB ---:Color_2}

In addition, the replacement string may contain a specifier
formatting (e.g. %03d) to be inserted into the resulting
sequence number string (self-incrementing counter),
as well as directives for text recoding

{xlt^c[s]:Color_2},

where s is a substring or group;
c - one of the following characters:

U Uppercase
L Lowercase
E QWERTY
R YTSUKEN
I Capitalize
H Hex
T Translit (Volapyuk)
W Translit to Cyrillic
B Alternative Translit
G Alternative Translit to cyrillic
_ replacing spaces with underscores
^ replacing underscores with spaces
0..9 XLAT according to the table defined by the file {User decoders:DecoderList},
counting in order In and Out XLAT files

Examples of strings to replace:

{\0\2xlt^T[\1]\3:Color_2} - translation of group 1 to Volapyuk
{xlt^1[&]:Color_2} - translation of the entire substring according to the ALT2WIN table

To insert the current date/time into the resulting string, you can
use the {time^[s]:Color_2} directive,

where s is a string of date/time formatting specifiers, for example:

{time^[%04d.%02d.%02d %02d?%02d?%02d]:Color_2} - yyyy.mm.dd hh?nn?ss
{time^[%2#%02d/%1#%02d/%0#%02d %3#%02d_%4#%02d_%5#%02d]:Color_2} - dd/mm/yy hh_nn_ss
{time^[%$]:Color_2} - time in Hex format

If the Selected text option is enabled, the search is performed only in the selected area.
If the Search backward option is enabled, the search is performed in the reverse direction.
If the Prompt on replace option is enabled, a message will appear on the screen before each replacement.
a request appears:

ﾚﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄｿ
ｳ Replace this occurrence? ｳ
ｳ ｳ
ｳ [Yes] [No] [Cancel] ｳ
ﾀﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾙ

(Replace the found string ?
[ Yes ] [ No ] [ Cancel ]).

The Group Undo flag determines how the {Undo:EUndo} command is executed.
(restore all replacements at once or one by one).

See also {Find}

  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ

{ Increment :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ

{ Decrement :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ

  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Change command allows you to change the current value of a register.
The command brings up the Modify dialog box,
in which you specify a new value, for example, ip or $7F0E.

.topic WriteTo
{ Write to :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Write to command allows you to save the contents of a memory block to a file.
The command opens a dialog box where you specify the start address.
and the end of the memory block within the current segment, for example, 0000:0F0A,
and then the {Write block to file:FileDialog} dialog box, using
which you can select the name of the file being created.

.topic ReadFrom
{ ReadFrom :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The ReadFrom to command allows you to fill a block of memory with the contents of a file.
The command calls the {Read block from:FileDialog} dialog box,
in which you specify the file name. The contents of the selected file
is read into the memory area corresponding to the current cursor position,
within a given segment.

{ATTENTION!!!:Color_4}
It is not recommended to execute the Read from command, as well as arbitrarily
change the contents of memory unless you know for sure,
What could this lead to?

.topic WUpdateASCII
{ WindowｳReload as ASCII (Alt+A) :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ

it if you do not want to save the changes you made.

If this command is received by the {Text viewer:TextViewer} window, it
closes and the {Text editor:ASCIIEditor} window opens in its place,
allowing you to edit the file being viewed.

.topic WUpdateHex
{ WindowｳReload as Hex (Alt+H) :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ

it if you do not want to save the changes you made.

If this command is received by the window {Hex viewer:HexViewer}, then it
closes and the {Hex editor:ASCIIEditor} window opens instead,
allowing you to fully edit the file being viewed.

.topic WWatch

  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ

.topic EnterWatch
Enter the parameter to display in the Watches window.

The format of the specifiers is: [-][nnn]X, where

[-] - optional minus sign,
indicating that the parameter will be left-aligned (by default, parameters
when displayed, they are aligned to the right);

[nnn] - optional decimal
length specifier in the range 1..255 (output of a field of length nnn characters;
0nnn - depending on the previous specifier on the right or left
zeros are added up to length nnn);

X - format symbol:

- 'm' means that the parameter
points to a buffer;
- 's' means that the parameter
points to a string;
- 'd' means decimal
representation of the Longint parameter;
- 'c' means that the younger one
parameter byte - character;
- 'x' means hexadecimal
representation of the Longint parameter.

For example, if the parameter points to a string containing 'spiny',
The following table shows the specifiers and their output:

ﾚﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄｿ
ｳ Specifier Result ｳ
 ﾃ ﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄ ｴ
ｳ 6s ' spiny' ｳ
ｳ -6s 'backs' ｳ
ｳ 3s 'iny' ｳ
ｳ -3s 'spi' ｳ
ｳ 06s '0spiny' ｳ
ｳ -06s 'spiny0' ｳ
ﾀﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾙ

.topicWatchWindow
{ Watches :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Watches window displays the program parameter values.
user in debug mode, entered by commands {Add watch:DAddWatch}
or {Edit watch:DEditWatch}. Press Ins to enter a new parameter,
Enter - to replace and Del - to delete the current parameter.

.topic WOutput
{ WindowｳOutput :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ

.topic OutputWindow
{ Output :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Output window displays the information output by the user program.
during execution of the procedures {Print string:PrintS} and {Print value:PrintV}.
The window can also respond to ANSI.SYS driver commands (lines,
containing Esc sequences, for example: [2J - clear screen).
You can scroll the contents of the window using the mouse or keyboard,
and resize it. Press Ctrl+Del to clear the window.

.topic CopyOutput
{ Copy :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Copy command in the {Output:OutputWindow} window copies the contents of the window.
in {Clipboard}.

.topic OOptions
The Options command displays the {Output options:OutputOptions} dialog box,
in which you can set the operating options of the {Output:OutputWindow} window.

.topic OutputOptions
{ Output options :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
When the Add Line Feed to carriage return option is enabled
(ASCII: 13) a newline character is added (ASCII: 10).

When the Add Return before newline option is enabled
(ASCII: 10) inserts a carriage return character (ASCII: 13).

When the Auto wrap option is enabled, automatic line wrapping occurs,
whose length exceeded the Columns value.

When the Destructive Backspace option is enabled, the Backspace symbol
(ASCII: 8) deletes the character before the cursor; otherwise
The cursor simply moves one position to the left.

The number of window columns (Columns) can take values from 1 to 132.
The number of window rows (Rows) can take values from 1 to 80.

.topic WMessage
{ WindowｳMessage (Alt+Home) :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Message command displays the {Message} window, which contains
the result of an external program running with the program enabled
Message options.

See also

{FileｳExecute:UExecute}
{Program list:ProgList}

.topic Message
{ Message window :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Message window contains the result of the external program,
performed with the Message option enabled. With it, you can
search for the required locations in files whose name is determined
either by the {$PATH, $NAME, $EXT:Directives} directives, or by setting
Filename mask and Line num mask filters. To find in a file
the desired line, select the line containing the file name in the Message window and
line number, and press Enter or Spacebar (to open a window
{Text viewer:TextViewer} instead of the {Text editor:ASCIIEditor} window
you need to hold down the Ctrl key). The Line num mask filter can consist of
two filters separated by a colon (row number and column number).
To use ':' in the filter body, it must be replaced with '::'.

For example, the GREP program, run with the -i+n+o+ options, returns
found lines in the form:

D:\DOC\TXT.DOC 53 Hello world !

The Filename mask and Line num mask filters for such lines will look like
respectively:

{$COPY(1," "):Color_2}
{$SEARCH(" [0-9]+"):Color_2}

See also

{Program list:ProgList}
{String filters:FilterDirectives}
{FileｳExecute:UExecute}

.topic WTerminal

.topic Terminal
{Terminal window:AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Terminal window is a terminal running in the mode
input/output of information via a serial port and controlled
commands compatible with the ANSI.SYS driver commands. The terminal also
supports various {protocols:Protocol} for transmitting and receiving files
commands {Upload} and {Download} and allows you to perform auto-dial
using the {Dial} command or {phone book:PhoneBook}.

See also {WindowｳBack:WBack}

files. When the Prompt on start flag is enabled, the Protocol dialog box
will always appear before the start of the transfer.

{Upload}
{Download}

.topic ModemSetup
{ Modem setup :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Modem setup command allows you to set command lines for the modem.
Command lines may contain the symbols | ^ v ~, respectively
meaning CR, DTR(On), DTR(Off), half-second delay.
\ before such a symbol tells the program that it needs
treat this symbol as a literal character, not as a specifier,
for example, \^. To indicate the \ character, it must be duplicated: \\.

{Init string:Color_2} - a string sent to the modem when a window is opened
terminal. The Init string is not sent if it is detected
Carrier Detect (CD) signal.

{Hangup string:Color_2} - a string sent to the modem when executing a command
{Hangup}, designed to break the connection.

{Answer string:Color_2} - a string sent to the modem when executing a command
{Answer}, designed to answer an incoming call.

{Cancel string:Color_2} - a string sent to the modem during automatic dialing for
move to the next number in the dialing list.

{Connect string:Color_2} - the string expected from the modem when connecting.
Used to exit the auto-dial when connected to one of the
answered numbers.

{Busy string:Color_2} - the string expected from the modem if the attempt fails
dialing a busy or unanswered number.

{Ring string:Color_2} - the string expected from the modem during a return call
auto-dial time.

{Break string:Color_2} - a string sent to the modem when it appears in the process
auto redial Ring string.

{Dial prefix:Color_2} - a string added before the number during auto-dialing.

{Dial suffix:Color_2} - a string added after the number during auto-dialing.

{Redial delay:Color_2} - time in seconds before sending the next message in the list
numbers for automatic dialing.

.topic TransferSetup
{ Transfer setup :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Transfer setup command allows you to set general settings.
{exchange protocol:Protocol} (General protocol options),
algorithm for {receiving files:Download} using the protocol
Zmodem (Zmodem options, Overwrite existing files), select
direction of movement of the slider when {reception:Download} and
{transfer:Upload} (Reverse progress bar - from right to left),
and also indicate the delay time (ms) between sending each
character and after the end of the line when executed in the {Terminal} window
{Paste:PasteTerminal} commands and when transferring files via protocol
ASCII (Delay between chars/lines).

.topic TOptions

.topic TerminalOptions
{Terminal options :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
When the Add Line Feed option is enabled, the carriage return character is added to the received carriage return character.
(ASCII: 13) a newline character is added (ASCII: 10).

When the Add Return option is enabled, before the accepted newline character
(ASCII: 10) inserts a carriage return character (ASCII: 13).

When the Auto wrap option is enabled, automatic line wrapping occurs,
whose length exceeded the Columns value.

When the Destructive Backspace option is enabled, the accepted Backspace character
(ASCII: 8) deletes the character before the cursor; otherwise
The cursor simply moves one position to the left.

When the Local echo option is enabled, transmitted characters are displayed in
in the {Terminal} window.

When the Strip option is enabled, the high bit of transmitted characters is discarded.
most significant bit (ASCII: 0..127).

When the Store lines in Back option is enabled, each line received
terminal, gets to the {Back:WBack} window.

If the Restore UART on close option is enabled, then when the device is closed
UART input/output is restored to its original state.

If the Drop modem on exit option is enabled, then when you exit the program or
When starting an external program, the modem is reset: DTR = RTS = 0.
When you close the Terminal window, the modem is always reset.

If the Raise modem on open option is enabled, then when you open a Terminal window
DTR and RTS port signals are set.

If the Ignore transfer errors option is enabled, then when errors occur

  UART receiver overrun
  UART receiver parity error
  UART receiver framing error
  No room for new char in buffer

a window with the corresponding error message will not appear.

The number of terminal columns (Columns) can take values 1..132.
The number of terminal lines (Rows) can take values from 1 to 80.

You can specify a file name in the Termcap name and Terminal type input lines.
TERMCAP and terminal type. If these lines are empty, the terminal supports
ANSI commands only.

In the input lines In XLAT file and Out XLAT file you can specify file names,
which store tables for converting input and output symbols
terminal streams. The table is an array of characters of size
256 bytes.
{Macro file:Color_X}
In the Macro file input line you can specify the name of the macro file
for {key reassignment:KeyReassign}. The Open button opens the specified
file in the macro editing dialog box {Macro list:MacrosDialog}.

.topic StatusWindow
Transferring file using {protocol:Protocol}. Press Esc to abort.

.topic OMode
{ OptionsｳCommunication :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Communication command displays the Communication parameters dialog box,
in which you set the parameters for transmitting and receiving information:

  device input - output (Device layer);
  address port (Port address); ﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄｿ
  number interrupts (IRQ number); ﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄ ﾅ optional
  vector interruptions port (COM vector); ﾄﾄﾄﾄﾙ
  IBM PC port (Port);
  speed transmission (Baud rate);
  Parity ;
  stop bits ;?
  size words (Data bits);
  hardware control (Hardware flow control);
  program control (Software flow control).

In addition, you can specify the sizes of the receive buffers (Input buffer size)
and transmission (Output buffer size) in the range of 1024..65520 Bytes.

.topic OKeyboard
{ OptionsｳKeyboard :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ

text in editor windows. By default, the speed is set to maximum.

.topic KbdDialog
{ Keyboard :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
ﾚﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄｿ
ｳ Vertical scroll speed ｳ
ｳ Fast Medium Slow ｳ
ｳ ｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱ ｳ
ﾀﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾙ

The Vertical scroll speed slider controls the speed of the vertical scroll
Scrolling text. You can move the slider using the keyboard arrows or the mouse.

The set value can be tested in the Speed tester window,
by pressing the Up and Down arrow keys.

If the Use INT 09 key handler flag is set, keystrokes will be
be handled by the standard keyboard interrupt handler;
In this case, the speed of vertical scrolling of the text will always remain unchanged.

If the Disable enhanced keys flag is set, the program will not
handle pressing "exotic" keys that are specific only to
for extended keyboards, such as Alt+Del, Alt+Home, Alt+End,
Alt+PgUp, Alt+PgDn, Alt+<, Alt+>, Alt+? and some others.

The Disable multiscrolling flag disables the mode in which it is possible
moving text simultaneously in several windows of the same type:

{text editors:ASCIIEditor};
{Hex editors:HexEditor};
{text viewer window:TextViewer};
{binary file viewer windows:HexViewer};
{windows for viewing .DBF files:DataViewer};
{HTML file viewer windows:HTMLViewer}.

This mode is toggled using the Scroll Lock key.

{ Mouse :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
ﾚﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄｿ
ｳ Mouse double click ｳ
ｳ Fast Medium Slow ｳ
ｳ ｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱｱ ｳ
ﾀﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾙ

The Mouse double click slider controls the double click speed.
You can move the slider using the keyboard arrows or the mouse.

ﾚﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄｿ
ｳ [X] Reverse mouse buttons ｳ
ﾀﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾙ

The Reverse mouse buttons option transfers the functions of the left mouse button to the right mouse button.
and vice versa.

ﾚﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄｿ

The Save/Restore position option allows you to restore the cursor position.
"mouse" written to the configuration file at the last exit.

ﾚﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄｿ
ｳ [X] Fast mouse reset ｳ
ﾀﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾙ

The Fast mouse reset option allows you to select a quick initialization method.
mouse drivers, which in some cases saves time when loading
programs.

ﾚﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄｿ
ｳ [X] Track mouse in menus ｳ
ﾀﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾙ

The Track mouse in menus option allows you to set the mode in which
Moving the mouse cursor over menu items immediately activates them
(in Windows 95 style).

ﾚﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄｿ
ｳ [X] Disable cursor masks ｳ
ﾀﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾙ

The Disable cursor masks option prohibits the use of special characters.
for the mouse cursor, intended to indicate those areas of the screen
programs in which clicking on the mouse button causes some kind of
actions such as changing the size or position of a window while capturing
its frame with the mouse cursor, etc.

ﾚﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄｿ
ｳ [X] Disable mouse usage ｳ
ﾀﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾙ

The Disable mouse usage option allows you to prohibit the use of the mouse.

ﾚﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄｿ
ｳ [X] Left click drags ｳ
ﾀﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾙ

The Left click drags option allows you to use a single left mouse button click
to start the {Drag-And-Drop:DragAndDrop} operation in the {File Manager:Panel} window.

ﾚﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄｿ
ｳ [X] Right click tags ｳ
ﾀﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾙ

The Right click tags option allows you to use the right mouse button.
to select items in the {File Manager:Panel} window list.

The Reset command reinitializes the mouse driver.

provided by default. If the Ctrl key is pressed,
default colors are set only for the current group or only

under the name selected in the {Store palette:FileDialog} dialog box.

Colors window by pressing the Enter key or the OK button.

.topic OEditOptions
{ OptionsｳEditor :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ

.topic EditOptions
{ Editor options :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
In the Editor options dialog box you can:

enable or disable the creation of .BAK files by the editor when
executing the command {Save:FSave} (Create backup files);

{note:Color_5} if in the directory of the saved file
there is a BAK subdirectory, backup files will be
be created in this subdirectory without changing their extension.
If there is no such subdirectory, then before saving the existing one
The file will be renamed to a file with the .BAK extension.
When working with files that have the same name but different
extensions such as .CPP and .HPP, it is recommended to keep backups
copies of files in the BAK subdirectory to avoid overwriting files;

set insert or replace mode;

set automatic line alignment mode to left
(Autoindent mode);

enable or disable the use of tab characters when writing to a file
(Use tab characters);

enable or disable the use of extended memory (EMS or XMS) for
Editor swap file (it is not recommended to use EMS or XMS if
it is small, and the files being edited are large, or if the running
the external program itself uses EMS or XMS);

enable or disable confirmation when opening a non-existent file
(Prompt on new file);

enable or disable automatic changing of the current directory
when opening the editor window (Change dir on open);

Allow or disallow the position of the opening window {cascade:WCascade}
(Cascade new window);

determine what will appear in the {Find} and {Replace} windows: word
at the position of the editor cursor or the previous search line
(Find text at cursor);

allow or prohibit (to save memory) the execution of operations
{Undo:EUndo} and {Redo:ERedo} (Enable Undo/Redo);

enable or disable the current line wrapping when typing
its length will exceed the maximum allowed length specified by the value
Max line width (Enable text wrap);

Enable hyphenation
(if the previous option Enable text wrap is set);

enable or disable the expansion of the transferred line by spaces up to the length
Max line width (Expand wrapped line) (if Enable option is set
text wrap);

enable or disable syntax highlighting of text in files with
.CBS extension and color highlighting of remarks in any files
(Syntax highlight);

enable or disable highlighting of the row/column where the cursor is located
(Highlight current line/column);

enable or disable highlighting of lines ending with
printed page (Highlight page breaks);

enable or disable highlighting of text boundaries defined by left indentation
and the maximum line length (Highlight >boundaries<);

set or disable the mode in which the block is marked in the window
the editor disappears on any action except continuing to mark
using Shift+arrow keys or mouse (Non-persistent blocks);

set or disable the mode in which the marked block is always
is replaced by the entered character or a new one inserted from {Clipboard}
the block is always deleted when pressing the Del, Backspace keys
(Overwrite blocks);

enable or disable positioning the cursor at the end of the selected block
after performing the Paste and Read block from file operations
(Paste goes to the end of the block);

set or disable the mode in which spaces are preserved
at the end of lines (Keep trailing blanks);

set or disable the mode in which, while reading the text
from the file all lines with a length exceeding the maximum
(Max line width), automatically word wrap
(Wrap lines on Load);

set or disable the mode in which non-empty lines
are written to the file without line ending characters CR/LF
(Unwrap lines on Save);

set or disable the mode in which at the end of the created
file always writes end-of-line characters CR/LF
(Write CR/LF at the end);

set or disable the mode in which at the end of the created
The end-of-file character (ASCII 26) is always written to the file
(Write EOF char at the end);

set the number of spaces replaced by the tab character (Tab size);

set the left margin when moving to a new line (Left margin);

set the maximum line length for automatic text wrapping
(Max line width);

set word delimiters; empty string - Default;

set keywords indicating a comment for the syntax
highlighting remarks in a text editor depending on the name and extension
the file being edited, as well as all the above parameters for the file group
in the {Editor group list:CommentDlg} dialog box (Groups button);

customize editor windows to react as desired when pressing various keys
in the {Editor keys:EditorKeysDialog} dialog box (Keys button).

.topic CommentDlg
{ Editor group list :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Editor group list dialog box allows you to specify keywords,
indicating a comment, for syntactic highlighting of remarks in the text
editor depending on the name and extension of the file being edited,
and also {editor options:EditOptions} for a group of files.

The Modify command brings up the {Modify item:NewComment} dialog box,
in which you can change the group mask or keyword.

The New command brings up the {New item:NewComment} dialog box,
which allows you to include a new item in the File names list.

The Options command displays the {Editor options:EditOptions} dialog box,
which allows you to change the editor options for the selected group.
The Ctrl+Options command sets the options specified for the selected group.
command {OptionsｳEditor:OEditOptions}.

The Files command displays the {Auxiliary file names:EditGroupNames} dialog box.

The Printer command displays the {Printer setup:PrinterSetup} dialog box.
The Ctrl+Printer command sets the options specified for the selected group
with the command {OptionsｳPrinter:OPrinter}.

The Delete command removes an item from the File names list.

The {Adjust:NewItemPos} command allows you to move an item to a different location.
on the list.

 ｺ                               ｺ

 ｺ    ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ         ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ  ｺ
 ﾈﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｼ

.topic EditorKeysDialog
In the Editor keys dialog box you can set the editor window settings,
affecting its behavior when certain keys are pressed:

set or disable the input mode for any characters, including
controls, as if you pressed {Ctrl+P:CtrlPPressed} every time
(Literal key input);

enable or disable cursor movement across non-empty positions
characters of the previous line when you press the Tab key
(Enable smart tab cursor movement);

enable or disable single-click paired character input mode
keys, for example, (), [], "" (Add matching chars);

set or disable the automatic space input mode after
punctuation marks ',', '.', ':', ';', '!', '?' (Auto-spaces after stops);

allow or disallow cursor movement between the first non-empty
symbol and the beginning of the line when you press the Home key
(Home goes to first non-blank character);

enable or disable closing editor windows when pressing a key
Esc (Esc closes);

allow or prohibit the replacement of keys previously intended for
cursor controls (^A, ^C, ^D, ^E, ^F, ^R, ^S, ^V, ^W, ^X, ^Z) on
standard commands Select all, Copy, Incremental search, Find,
Replace, Save, Paste, Cut, Undo, and Ctrl+Home/End key replacements
to Ctrl+PgUp/PgDn and vice versa.

{OptionsｳFile Manager :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ

{File Manager:Panel} windows:

When the flag is enabled, the copy mode with optimal filling is possible
discs (Optimal Fill);

disable automatic correction of TREEINFO files when created,

Disable working with the standard definition file CONNECT.MSK when displaying

{OptionsｳFile ManagerｳClear the Unfold flag on dir change:Color_X}
set the mode in which the {Unfold subdirectories:Unfold} flag is always
resets when moving to another directory, which allows you to avoid

always convert the name of the created directory to uppercase;
This may be relevant when working in a DOS window of the operating system.
Windows 95 (Create directories in uppercase);
{OptionsｳFile ManagerｳIncremental search options:Color_X}
select the mode of sequential search of files (directories) by letters
name (Incremental search options): if the Case sensitive option is set,
then to search for directories you need to press capital letters;
If the Ignore Cyrillic option is set, then Russian letters are accepted
as the corresponding Latin ones, for example, ? = q, ? = D, etc.;
If the Alt/Ctrl activates/aborts options are set, then enable/disable
search mode occurs when you press Alt or Ctrl respectively;
{OptionsｳFile ManagerｳFile compare options:Color_X}
select the method for comparing the contents of directories in panels when running

select the mode of automatic rereading of the contents of the displayed

  Modified only - automatically
reread only those catalogs,
which have changed since the file
operations Copy, RenMov, MkDir, Delete;
  Always - automatically
reread all the catalogues;
  Never - prohibit automatic
rereading; at the same time refresh
The contents of the panels can only be
manually, for example, by pressing {Ctrl+R:ReRead};

set a symbol to mark selected files/directories (Tag character);

set the pause time after which in Tree mode and enabled
the Auto change directory flag, as well as in {Quick view:QuickView} modes

opposite panel (Auto change delay);

set the name mask, color, and group index for highlighting and sorting

specify the names of the Dirinfo and Description files, and also specify the number of spaces

.topic NewGroup

  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The New item / Modify item dialog box allows you to set a file name mask,

and also set the group index (1..255) used for sorting.
Different groups can have the same index, and the files in the panel

will not be shown in the panel. When the Directory flag is enabled, the selected
The settings will be relative to a group of directories, not files.

.topic FMFilesDialog
In the File Manager files dialog box you can:

specify a list of file names that contain directory information
(`Dirinfo' files);

specify a list of description file names (Description files)
(see also {Show file descriptions:FilesBBS});

set the number of spaces between the file name, expanded to 12 characters,
and its description, used in copying and renaming operations
and editing files with descriptions (Whitespaces between file name and
description) (if there is a zero value between the file name and its description
there will always be one space regardless of the length of the name);

enable or disable the removal of extra spaces and line breaks
(CR, LF) from the description text when copying it
(Remove extra spaces from description text).

.topic FMKeysDialog
In the File Manager keys dialog box you can set the desired
the reaction of the {File Manager:Panel} window panels to clicking on some
service keys:

enable or disable automatic cursor movement down
one line when selecting files with the Insert key (Ins moves down);

Allow or disallow switching to the parent directory when clicking on
the Backspace key if the input line {Prompt:PromptLine} is empty
(Backspace goes to upper directory);

enable or disable turning panels on/off when clicking
the Esc key in the same way as when pressing the keys {Ctrl+O:TogglePanels},
if the Prompt input line is empty (Esc toggles panels on/off);

enable or disable the Delete command when clicking
the Del key is the same as pressing the F8 key
(Del erases files and directories);

enable or disable file selection when pressing a key
Space is the same as pressing the Ins key if the Prompt input line is
empty (Space selects/unselects items);
{OptionsｳFile ManagerｳKeys:Color_X}
enable or disable the use of the left and right Ctrl keys for
control of the left and right Drive selector respectively; when pressed
the Shift key treats this flag as the opposite
(Drive selectors sensitive to Left/Right Ctrl keys);

Allow or deny opening of all files selected in the panel
for editing when executing the Open command
(F4/Ctrl+F4 opens focused file only);

enable or disable switching by pressing Alt+Ctrl keys,
which displays in a pop-up window (Mouse hint)
the name of the file or directory where the mouse cursor is located
(Alt+Ctrl displays names under mouse cursor);

enable or disable the calculation and display of the size of the selected
directory when you press the Space key (Space calculates selected
directory size);

enable or disable automatic cursor movement down
one line when calculating and displaying the size of the selected
directory by pressing Alt+F3 (Alt+F3 on directory moves down);

enable or disable the sequential search mode
files (directories) by letters of the name by pressing the first letter and simultaneously
holding down the Caps Lock key (CapsLock+character activates incremental search);

enable or disable the display of the extended status bar with
additional commands and hot keys F9 - Menu, F10 - Exit.
{Macro file:Color_X}
In the Macro file input line you can specify the name of the macro file
for {key reassignment:KeyReassign}. The Open button opens the specified
file in the macro editing dialog box {Macro list:MacrosDialog}.

.topic OUserOptions

select the method of interrupting the user program during execution

.topic OvrOptions
{ OptionsｳOverlay :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Overlay command displays the Overlay options dialog box, where you can
You can change the default overlay loading parameters.
program code, as well as the size of the overlay buffer.

The Use expanded/extended memory flag determines whether to load the overlay
code into extended memory (if your machine configuration allows it).

When the Move buffer to upper memory (UMB) flag is enabled, the program
will attempt to place the overlay buffer in the UMB (if there is a free block)
of the required size), and not in Conventional memory. This will free up space for
work memory block of a size equal to the size of the overlay buffer (see below).
{ATTENTION!:Color_4}
Placing the overlay buffer in UMB may cause conflicts or
system freezes when launching some external programs.

The Use upper memory (UMB) flag for Heap enables or disables the use of
UMB blocks for placing various dynamically created objects and
data during program execution. This flag has no direct effect
relation to the work of the overlay mechanism, but together with the previous flag
It allows the most flexible use of UMB either for overlay only
buffer, either only for the dynamic memory manager to work, or for
for both at the same time.

Overlay preferences switches allow you to choose the most optimal
How to use extended memory:

  Use EMS only - use EMS only
  Use XMS only - use XMS only
  Use EMS over XMS - first try EMS
  Use XMS over EMS - first try XMS

Overlay read options switches allow you to select the most optimal
Method for loading overlay code into extended memory:

  Load all segments at the start -
load all overlay code in
extended memory when starting the program

  Load segments at run-time as needed -
load parts of the overlay code into
expanded memory as needed

The overlay buffer size can be set within the range
90,000...150,000 bytes. The larger the buffer, the less free memory.
remains the same as the program, but the operating speed is slightly higher.
The optimal size is 105000 bytes, which is set by default.

{ATTENTION!:Color_4}
The changes are written directly to the CONNECT.EXE file and will manifest themselves
only after restarting the program.

You can set the event log options. "Event Log" -
this is a file named Log file name, in which all lines are written,
appearing on the screen when performing any actions, as well as the time
events, for example:

- 11:15:25 Loading MYFILE.TXT.
+ 11:16:09 Copying MYFILE.TXT to E:\1.DOC.
! 11:16:10 Error. Could not create E:\1.DOC.

When you open a file, the current date and time are written into it in the format,
determined by the settings of the {Country settings:OCountry} dialog.

Options:

  Enable event logging -
to keep or not to keep an "event log";

  Read from disk (-)
  Write to disk (+)
* * * * *
  Other events ( ) -
classes of events that can be
to record or not to record
in the "magazine".

.topic PrinterSetup
{Printer setup :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
In the Printer setup dialog box you can:

specify the name of the device to which the output will be carried out
printing text, for example, LPT2 or D:\TEMP\DUMP.PRN (file on disk).
If no name is specified, the device on LPT1 is used by default.
(Prn device name);

set the name of the font file for graphic printing (Font file name);

enable or disable graphic printing using a font file
(Use external font (Graphics mode));

set high quality graphic printing
(Bold characters (Double strike));

enable page-by-page printing mode (Force page breaks (eject pages));

set the string sent to the device before printing starts (Init string);

set the left (Left margin), top (Top margin) and bottom margins
(Bottom margin), as well as the number of lines per page (Lines per page);

set the print interval (Interval between lines) in the range 1.00..3.54;

set the number of characters printed per program cycle
in the background (Chars per cycle).

If the page-by-page printing mode is enabled and the number of lines per page is not specified
or equal to zero, it is determined automatically depending on the interval
printing and indents at the top and bottom.

program keys, but generated when executing a macro press

or running {external program:ProgList}.

{key sequence input mode:HotKeyList}.
To finish entering the sequence, press the Stop button.
or Ctrl+Break keys.

The Remove command removes the current key from the Keys list.

The Clear all command clears the entire list.

The Move up and Move down commands are used to change the sequence
keys in the list.

Using the Keyboard state and Check keyboard state switches
You can enable or disable the keyboard status check.
when comparing the codes of the pressed keys with the codes of which
the sequence consists of.

.topic UserDialog
{ New macro / Modify macro :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The New macro / Modify macro dialog box contains:

  line input (Title)
  Hot key selector and Hot keys button
  list commands?
  list contents macro (Contents)
  Command, Key, String, Repeat, Delete buttons

The Title input line contains the name of the macro.

Using the {Hot key:KeyView} selector, you can set the following for this macro:
"hotkey" for quick access. If you want to call a macro
by pressing several keys in sequence, you need to use
Hot keys button that opens a dialog box
{Macro hot key sequence:HotKeyListDlg}.

The Commands list contains all available commands of the program,
corresponding to the menu items, as well as the commands generated when
by pressing the Yes, No, OK, Cancel buttons.

The Command command places the selected item in the Contents list.
position of the current command. If the current command is Pause, then it is necessary
Set the delay duration in milliseconds. If the delay is zero, the macro will be executed.
pauses until Alt+F8 is pressed.

The Key command displays the {Macro key:KeyView} dialog box,
which allows you to include a new key in the macro.

The String command displays the {Macro string:MacroInputBox} dialog box,
which allows you to include a sequence in a macro
pressing the keys corresponding to the characters of the entered string.

The Repeat command allows you to set the number of repetitions of the command selected in the list.
Command contents (1..65535).

The Delete command removes the command selected in the Contents list from the macro.

.topic MacrosDialog
{ Macro list :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Macro list dialog box contains:

  list macros user (Macros)
  list contents macro (Contents)
  buttons Run, Repeat, File, Modify, New, Delete, Adjust

The Macros list contains previously created and saved in a file
user macros.

The Contents list contains all commands of the current macro and is updated
when selecting a new macro.

The Run and Repeat commands execute the selected macro (the Repeat command -
the specified number of times).

The File command allows you to write the current list of macros to another
file or load a new list from another file.

The Modify command displays the {Modify macro:UserDialog} dialog box,
in which you can change the name of the macro, its contents, and also
reassign the macro call key.

The New command displays the {New macro:UserDialog} dialog box,
which allows you to create and include a new macro in the Macros list.

The Delete command removes the selected macro from the Macros list.

The {Adjust:NewItemPos} command allows you to move a macro to a different location.
on the list.
