.topic Directives
{ Command line macros :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ {$PATH:Color_X} {$NAME:Color_X} {$EXT:Color_X}
Directives {$PATH:Color_2}, {$NAME:Color_2}, {$EXT:Color_2}
(for long file names - {$LPATH:Color_2}, {$LNAME:Color_2},
{$LEXT:Color_2}) substitute the corresponding values into the command line
components of the name of the file opened in the current editor window,
or the file on which the cursor of the active panel of the {File Manager:Panel} window is located.

For example, the line

D:\TASM\TASM.EXE $PATH$NAME$EXT /R/ZI

will be converted to a string

D:\TASM\TASM.EXE D:\WORK\ASM\MYPROG.ASM /R/ZI
ｳ ｳ ｳ
ｳ (file name) ｳ
ｳﾄﾄﾄﾄ(command line)ﾄﾄﾄﾄｳ
{$OPATH:Color_X} {$ONAME:Color_X} {$OEXT:Color_X}
Directives {$OPATH:Color_2}, {$ONAME:Color_2}, {$OEXT:Color_2}
(for long file names - {$LOPATH:Color_2}, {$LONAME:Color_2},
{$LOEXT:Color_2}) substitute the corresponding values into the command line
components of the file name on which the cursor is located opposite
current window panel {File Manager:Panel}.
{$LEFT:Color_X} {$RIGHT:Color_X} {$OPPOSITE:Color_X}
Directives {$LEFT:Color_2}, {$RIGHT:Color_2}, {$OPPOSITE:Color_2}
(for long file names - {$LLEFT:Color_2}, {$LRIGHT:Color_2}, {$LOPP:Color_2})
substitute the names of the directories opened in the command line, respectively
in the left, right, or opposite current panel of the {File Manager:Panel} window.
{$CN:Color_X}
The {$CN:Color_2} directive substitutes the directory name into the command line,
in which the CONNECT.EXE file is located.
{$CURDIR:Color_X}
The {$CURDIR:Color_2} directive substitutes the name into the command line
current directory (for long names - {$LCURDIR:Color_2}).
{$SWAPDIR:Color_X}
The {$SWAPDIR:Color_2} directive substitutes the path specified in the command line
{OptionsｳSetupｳSwap file directory:OSetup}.
{$DIRARC:Color_X}
The {$DIRARC:Color_2} directive substitutes the current path into the command line.
the archive being viewed (without the archive name).
{$DIRNAME:Color_X}
The directive {$DIRNAME():Color_2} substitutes into the command line
only the name (and extension, if any) of the directory specified in brackets.
Any directive that returns can be passed as a directory.
directory name, for example, {$PATH:Directives}.
{$SEL:Color_X}
Directive {$SEL:Color_2} (for long file names - {$LSEL:Color_2})
on the command line writes to the SELECTED.LST file created in the same
directory as the Swap file, the names of the files selected in the window panels
{File Manager:Panel}. You can specify a different name for this in brackets.
file, for example: {$SEL(D?\TEMP\SEL.LST):Color_2}. This mechanism
allows you to pass to running programs, such as archivers,
list of files:

D:\PACK\PKZIP.EXE -BD:\ -A -P {$PROMPT:Directives}(-ex $PATH$NAME) @$SEL
{$SLAPPEND:Color_X} {$SLATTR:Color_X} {$SLBKSLSH:Color_X} {$SLDMASK:Color_X} {$SLPATH:Color_X} {$SLPREFIX:Color_X} {$SLQUOTES:Color_X} {$SLSIZE:Color_X} {$SLSKIPD:Color_X} {$SLSUFFIX:Color_X} {$SLTIME:Color_X} {$SLTMASK:Color_X}
Directives {$SLPATH:Color_2}, {$SLSIZE:Color_2}, {$SLTIME:Color_2},
{$SLATTR:Color_2}, {$SLSKIPD:Color_2}, {$SLBKSLSH:Color_2}, {$SLQUOTES:Color_2},
{$SLAPPEND:Color_2}, {$SLDMASK():Color_2}, {$SLTMASK():Color_2},
{$SLPREFIX():Color_2}, {$SLSUFFIX():Color_2}
can be used in conjunction with the {$SEL:Color_2} directive to control
format of lines in the created file.
{$REPORT:Color_X}
The {$REPORT:Color_2} directive substitutes the file name into the command line,
to which the output of the program being launched is redirected when the flag is enabled
Message.
{$CMD:Color_X}
The {$CMD:Color_2} directive is designed to create a cmd file from the contents
Command line. You can specify the name of the file being created in brackets,
for example, {$CMD(D?\TEMP\CMD.TXT):Color_2}. If the name is not specified, it is created
CONNECT.CMD file in the same directory as the Swap file. This can be
used to run various programs with long strings under Windows
(more than 128 bytes) using command lines. It is convenient to use the run.exe utility,
allowing you to execute a cmd file and redirect stdout and stderror to the running
programs to the specified file. For example:

Program path: run /a+{$REPORT: Directives} {$MSG:Directives}
Command line:
PIC\bin\picc.exe -E -O -G -Zg -INTEL -D24 -ASMLIST
-M$LPATH$LNAME.map -{$PROMPT:Directives}(16F73 -DB400 -RESROMFFA-FFF -L-Pid=ffah)
$LPATH$LNAME$LEXT $CMD

This example allows you to run the compiler using the run.exe utility.
picc, redirecting all its output to the existing $REPORT file, the contents of which
which will be shown in the {Message} window when the program finishes running.
{$XNT:Color_X}
The {$XNT:Color_2} directive is designed to launch applications and open
files using Windows NT. Learn more about {using the $XNT:NT_Exec directive}
and about {working under Windows NT:CN_NT}.
{$FNAME:Color_X}
Directive {$FNAME:Color_2} (for long file names - {$LFNAME:Color_2})
on the command line calls {file dialog:FileDialog}. In brackets
You can specify the source string, for example: {$FNAME(D?\SOURCE.TXT):Color_2}.
{$FINDNAME:Color_X}
The {$FINDNAME():Color_2} directive substitutes the full name into the command line.
the file specified in brackets, if it is located in at least one of the directories,
specified by the PATH environment variable.
{$FINDDIR:Color_X}
The {$FINDDIR():Color_2} directive inserts the path to the file into the command line,
specified in brackets if the file is located in at least one of the directories,
specified by the PATH environment variable.
{$FIND1ST:Color_X}
Directive {$FIND1ST():Color_2} (for long file names - {$LFIND1ST():Color_2})
substitutes the short or long name of the first file into the command line,
found using the mask specified in brackets, for example: {$FIND1ST(*.TXT):Color_2}.
{$CLIP:Color_X} {$WINCLIP:Color_X}
The {$CLIP():Color_2} and {$WINCLIP():Color_2} directives are used to copy
the text specified in brackets in {Clipboard} or
MS Windows Clipboard. Other directives can be specified in brackets,
for example: {$CLIP($NAME$EXT):Color_2}.
{$PUT:Color_X}
The {$PUT():Color_2} directive writes to a text file with the specified name.
a string consisting of a key and a value separated by the '=' symbol.
If such a file does not exist, it is created. If the file already contains such a key,
its value is replaced with a new one. The syntax of the directive:

$PUT(D:\TEMP\CN.TMP<Settings=COM2,9600,N,2,8)
ｳ ｳ ｳ ｳ ｳ ｳ
ｳ(file name) ｳ ｳ(key)ｳ ｳ (value) ｳ
ｳ ｳ
ｳ(line to be written) ｳ

The presence of the '<' symbol after the file name is mandatory.
{$GET:Color_X}
The {$GET():Color_2} directive reads from a text file with the specified name.
the value corresponding to the given key and substitutes it into the command
string instead of itself. Directive syntax:

$GET(D:\TEMP\CN.TMP>Settings)
ｳ ｳ ｳ ｳ
ｳ(file name) ｳ ｳ(key)ｳ

The presence of the '>' symbol after the file name is mandatory.
{$PRINT:Color_X}
The {$PRINT():Color_2} directive places a file with the name specified in brackets
in {printer queue:Spooler}. You can pass the name on the command line
XLAT file, as well as the /B switch, which enables the Binary printing mode.
{$WRBLK:Color_X} {$RDBLK:Color_X}
The directives {$WRBLK():Color_2} and {$RDBLK():Color_2} serve respectively to
records of the block selected in the {text editor:ASCIIEditor} window in
the file specified in brackets and replacing the selected block with the contents
the specified file by deleting the allocated block and reading
file contents to the position of the editor cursor. This mechanism allows
run external programs that process a part in a certain way
editable text, for example, recoders:

$WRBLK(BLK.TXT) D:\UTIL\ENCODE.EXE BLK.TXT; $RDBLK(BLK.TXT)
{$WORD:Color_X}
The {$WORD:Color_2} directive inserts the word under the cursor into the command line.
in the current editor window.
{$HREF:Color_X}
The {$HREF:Color_2} directive substitutes the current text into the command line.
links in the current window {HTML viewer:HTMLViewer}.
{$PROMPT:Color_X}
The {$PROMPT:Color_2} directive on the command line displays a dialog box
{Program arguments:PromptDialog}. You can specify the source code in brackets.
a line, for example: {$PROMPT(File):Color_2}, and also your own line name
input and your own dialog box title, for example:

$PROMPT($PATH$NAME$EXT,~E~nter file names to compare,Compare two files)
ｳ ｳ ｳ ｳ ｳ ｳ
Input data Input line label Dialog title
{$ENV:Color_X}
The {$ENV():Color_2} directive substitutes a variable into the command line
environment corresponding to the string specified in brackets, for example:
{$ENV(COMSPEC):Color_2}.
{$SET:Color_X}
The {$SET():Color_2} directive adds a new color or modifies an existing color.
environment variable, for example:

$SET(TEMP=C:\TEMP)
$SET(PATH={$ENV:Directives}(PATH);;{$PATH:Directives})

Directives {$YEAR:Color_2}, {$FYEAR:Color_2}, {$MONTH:Color_2},
{$DAY:Color_2}, {$HOUR:Color_2}, {$MIN:Color_2}, {$SEC:Color_2},
{$MSEC:Color_2} are replaced with the corresponding components
current date/current time.
{$HIST:Color_X}
The {$HIST:Color_2} directive on the command line causes
{command history window:PromptHistory}.
{$FILTER:Color_X}
The {$FILTER():Color_2} directive reads from the file specified in brackets
Advanced filter settings previously saved using the Store command
dialog box {Advanced panel filter:AdvancedFilter} and passes them
active panel of the window {File Manager:Panel}. If the file name is not specified
(empty string), the directive disables the Advanced filter mode.
{$MAC:Color_X}
The {$MAC():Color_2} directive opens a dialog box
{Macro list:MacrosDialog} with a list of macros stored in the specified
in brackets file, for example:

$MAC({$CN:Directives}\EDITKEYS.MAC)
{$PRG:Color_X}
The {$PRG():Color_2} directive opens the {Program list:ProgList} dialog box.
with the list of programs stored in the file specified in brackets. If after
the file name contains a number (1..n), the program list cursor will be set
to the corresponding list element, for example:

$PRG({$CN:Directives}\ARCMENU.PRG 4)

This mechanism allows you to create nested lists of programs stored
in different files and go to the Program list dialog box from one
list to another and back, simply by pressing the Enter key.
{$MENU:Color_X}
The {$MENU():Color_2} directive opens a dialog box
{User menu:UserMenuDlg} with the list of programs stored in the specified
in brackets file.
{$VM:Color_X} {$XM:Color_X}
The directives {$VM():Color_2} and {$XM():Color_2} set respectively
for the program itself and for external programs launched, the display video mode
by the number indicated in brackets (1..255), for example:

$VM(86) (set video mode to 132 x 60 resolution).

To restore the previous video mode, you need to execute this directive
with a zero parameter: $VM(0), or execute the command
{EGA/VGA lines:OEGALines} (Alt+F6).
{$KBD:Color_X}
The {$KBD():Color_2} directive places key scan codes into the keyboard buffer,
indicated in brackets. For example, two directives

$KBD($1800) $KBD(Omyconfig)

correspond to successive keystrokes

Alt+OO myconfig

Maximum number of scan codes placed in the keyboard buffer
must not exceed the buffer size (default 15).
{$MEM:Color_X}
The {$MEM():Color_2} directive on the command line defines the memory size
(KByte) that needs to be allocated to the program being launched. In the case where
the program runs in Swap mode, and there is more free memory,
than indicated in brackets, the None mode is selected, which is significant
speeds up the operation:

D:\PACK\PKZIP.EXE $MEM(100)
{$MSG:Color_X} {$MSG(FilterName):Color_X}
The {$MSG:Color_2} directive enables the Message flag. You can specify a name in parentheses.
a filter program used to translate strings output by the running
program to the standard output device, in the required format,
For example:

AIN V -p1 $MSG(FAIN)

Here FAIN.EXE is a program that converts the output of the AIN archiver into
format accepted by the internal archive viewer.
{$ERR:Color_X}
The {$ERR:Color_2} directive, when the Message flag is enabled, reassigns
output of the running program to the standard error device (StdErr)
in the same file as the $MSG directive.
{$NOMSGWIN:Color_X}
The {$NOMSGWIN:Color_2} ({$NMW:Color_2}) directive when the Message flag is enabled
prevents the {Message} window from opening after the startup program has finished
programs.
{$USERSCR:Color_X}
The {$USERSCR:Color_2} ({$USR:Color_2}) directive when the Message flag is enabled
Switches the program screen to the user's screen.
{$NOREDRAW:Color_X} {$NOREREAD:Color_X}
Directives {$NOREDRAW:Color_2} ({$NRD:Color_2}) and {$NOREREAD:Color_2}
({$NRR:Color_2}) prevent screen refresh and directory rereading
panels of the {File Manager:Panel} window after returning from the launched program.
{$NTM:Color_X}
The {$NTM:Color_2} (No transfer message) directive prevents the appearance of
Transfer window before launching the program.
{$VIEW:Color_X} {$XVIEW:Color_X} {$DBASE:Color_X} {$HTML:Color_X} {$EDIT:Color_X} {$XEDIT:Color_X}
Directives {$VIEW:Color_2}, {$XVIEW:Color_2}, {$DBASE:Color_2},
{$HTML:Color_2}, {$EDIT:Color_2}, {$XEDIT:Color_2} mean that
when executing the View file command (F3, Alt+F3, Shift+F3) in the window
{File Manager:Panel} you need to open the {Text viewer:TextViewer} window,
{Hex viewer:HexViewer}, {dBASE viewer:DataViewer},
{HTML viewer:HTMLViewer}, {Text editor:ASCIIEditor} or
{Hex editor:HexEditor}.
{$SAMEWIN:Color_X}
The {$SAMEWIN:Color_2} directive means that when the command is executed
View file (F3, Alt+F3, Shift+F3) in the {File Manager:Panel} window
use the already open window {Text viewer:TextViewer},
{Hex viewer:HexViewer}, {dBASE viewer:DataViewer},
{HTML viewer:HTMLViewer}, {Text editor:ASCIIEditor} or
{Hex editor:HexEditor}, if any.
{$ARC:Color_X}
The {$ARC:Color_2} directive means that the selected file should be expanded
in the File Manager window panel as an archive.
{$PANEL:Color_X}
The {$PANEL:Color_2} directive means that the selected file should be expanded
in the File Manager window pane as a list containing file names and
catalogs.
{$ICON:Color_X}
The {$ICON:Color_2} directive means that the selected file (.CBB or .PRG)
needs to be loaded as a window {Icon:ULoadIcon}.
{$HELP:Color_X}
The {$HELP:Color_2} directive opens the selected file (.HLP) for viewing.
in the Help window.
{$XW:Color_X} {$XX:Color_X}
The directives {$XW:Color_2} and {$XX:Color_2} execute for the specified in brackets
file program or command associated with this name in the lists
{Viewer list:ViewDlg} and {File associations:ExtDlg} respectively.

.topic FilterDirectives
{ String filters :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
Filters {$COPY:Color_2}, {$SEARCH:Color_2}, {$POS:Color_2} are replaced
to the parts of the string processed by the filter that correspond to their arguments.
{$COPY():Color_X}
The filter {$COPY():Color_2} has two arguments in the form of numeric values
the starting and ending positions in the original string, or in the form of enclosed
" " substrings between which the desired substring is located. " " can also
be a regular expression. If the substring can be considered as
{regular expression:RegExp}, then it is exactly this that is searched for.

So, for example, if the original string is:

D:\DOC\TXT.DOC 53 Hello world !

then a filter like $COPY(1," ") will return:

D:\DOC\TXT.DOC

i.e. all characters, starting from the first up to the first space encountered.
{$POS():Color_X}
The filter {$POS():Color_2} has one argument in the form
{regular expression:RegExp} enclosed in " ".
For the same string, a filter like $POS(" [0-9]+") will return 16
(the position of a space and a non-zero number of characters from 0 to 9 in a string).
{$SEARCH():Color_X}
The filter {$SEARCH():Color_2} has one argument in the form
{regular expression:RegExp} enclosed in " ".
For the same string, a filter like $SEARCH(" [0-9]+") will return 53
(space and a non-zero number of characters from 0 to 9).
If the regular expression contains groups, then the result of the filter is
will be the first group \0. For example, if the original string is:

C:\Pic\400.c: 2598: undefined identifier: ee_sa (error)

The filter $SEARCH("^.:\\[^:]*") will return C:\Pic\400.c, and the filter
To search for a row number, $SEARCH(":: ([0-9]+):: ") will return 2598.

All other characters in the filter string are returned unchanged.
So, a filter of the type

file $COPY(1," ") line($SEARCH(" [0-9]+"))

for the same string will return:

file D:\DOC\TXT.DOC line (53)

If the filter result should be a number, and in the original string it is specified in
In hex format, you need to add the $ symbol before the filter. For example, $$COPY(10,14).
{$UP():Color_X} {$DOWN():Color_X}
Macros {$UP():Color_2} and {$DOWN():Color_2} have one parameter in the form of a number
lines in the {Message} window to move up or down before
by using a filter containing them.
For example, for Turbo Pascal, the information output by the compiler about
errors, looks like this:

E:\WORK\CONNECT\1.PAS(2): Error 3: Unknown identifier.
kjhgkug
^
In order to be able to stand with the cursor on the line containing the error,
to open a window with the file that called it, you need to write:

Filename mask $UP(1)$COPY(1,"(")
Line num mask $UP(1)$COPY("(",")):$DOWN(1)$POS("\^")

.topic ProgList
{ Program list :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Program list dialog box contains:

  four lines input
(Program path, Command line,
Filename mask, Line num mask)
  list programs?
  switches (Main)
  switches (Setup)
  switches (Options)
  buttons Run, File, Modify, New,
Icon, Edit, Delete, Adjust

The Program path input line contains the name of the program or directive

{$ARC:Directives} {$DBASE:Directives} {$EDIT:Directives} {$HELP:Directives}
{$HTML:Directives} {$ICON:Directives} {$PANEL:Directives} {$SAMEWIN:Directives}
{$VIEW:Directives} {$XEDIT:Directives} {$XNT:Directives} {$XVIEW:Directives}
{$XW:Directives} {$XX:Directives}

The Command line input line may contain a command line,
passed to the program being launched. Directives can be used

{$CLIP:Directives} {$CMD:Directives} {$CN:Directives} {$CURDIR:Directives}
{$DAY:Directives} {$DIRARC:Directives} {$DIRNAME:Directives} {$ENV:Directives}
{$EXT:Directives} {$FILTER:Directives} {$FIND1ST:Directives} {$FINDDIR:Directives}
{$FINDNAME:Directives} {$FNAME:Directives} {$FYEAR:Directives} {$GET:Directives}
{$HIST:Directives} {$HOUR:Directives} {$HREF:Directives} {$KBD:Directives}
{$LEFT: Directives} {$MAC:Directives} {$MEM:Directives} {$MENU:Directives}
{$MIN:Directives} {$MONTH:Directives} {$MSEC:Directives} {$MSG:Directives}
{$NAME:Directives} {$NOMSGWIN:Directives} {$NOREDRAW:Directives} {$NOREREAD:Directives}
{$NTM:Directives} {$OEXT:Directives} {$ONAME:Directives} {$OPATH:Directives}
{$OPPOSITE:Directives} {$PATH:Directives} {$PRG:Directives} {$PRINT:Directives}
{$PROMPT:Directives} {$PUT:Directives} {$RDBLK:Directives} {$REPORT:Directives}
{$RIGHT:Directives} {$SEC:Directives} {$SEL:Directives} {$SET:Directives}
{$SLAPPEND:Directives} {$SLATTR:Directives} {$SLBKSLSH:Directives} {$SLDMASK:Directives}
{$SLPATH:Directives} {$SLPREFIX:Directives} {$SLQUOTES:Directives} {$SLSIZE:Directives}
{$SLSKIPD:Directives} {$SLSUFFIX:Directives} {$SLTIME:Directives} {$SLTMASK:Directives}
{$SWAPDIR:Directives} {$USERSCR:Directives} {$VM:Directives} {$WINCLIP:Directives}
{$WORD:Directives} {$WRBLK:Directives} {$XM:Directives} {$YEAR:Directives}

Input lines Filename mask, Line num mask can contain filters

{$COPY():FilterDirectives}, {$POS():FilterDirectives}, {$SEARCH():FilterDirectives}

and macros

{$DOWN():FilterDirectives}, {$UP():FilterDirectives},

allowing the {Message} window to determine the file name and line number from the text
(the Message switch must be on).

If Swap mode is selected, the main program will attempt to swap out a large
part of its code in XMS (Extended memory) or in EMS (Expanded memory),
or, if neither is possible, to a file on disk.
{ATTENTION!!!:Color_4}
This mode cannot be used to execute resident programs.

If the Unload mode is selected, the main program will completely release
the memory it occupies, providing it to the program being launched,
However, the return process will take a little longer.
{ATTENTION!!!:Color_4}
This mode must be used to execute resident programs.

If the None mode is selected, then the program being launched
approximately as much memory as shown will be provided
free memory indicator in the lower right corner of the screen at the moment
execution time of the operation, plus the size of the overlay buffer.
{ATTENTION!!!:Color_4}
This mode cannot be used to run resident
programs.

If the Save editor files switch is enabled
( [X] ),
then before starting the program the command {Save all:FSaveAll} will be executed.
It is recommended to always enable it if Unload mode is selected; otherwise
In this case, the changes you made will remain unsaved.

If the Save desktop switch is enabled
( [X] ),
then the command will be executed before starting the program
{Save desktop:OSaveOptions}.

If the Load Snipper switch is enabled
( [X] ),
then the resident utility {Snipper} will be loaded before starting the program.

If the Message switch is on
( [X] ),
then the result of the running program will appear in the {Message} window.

If the Load COMMAND.COM switch is enabled
( [X] ),
then another copy of COMMAND.COM will be downloaded.

If the Swap to disk switch is enabled
( [X] ),
then the code will always be unloaded to disk (in order to
the program being launched could fully utilize EMS or XMS).

The File command brings up a dialog box.
{Execute a file; load/store program list:FileDialog} with buttons
Run, Load, and Store. When the Run command is executed, the name of the selected file
will be entered into the Path input line. The Load command loads a new list.
programs from the selected file or opens an empty list if such
file does not exist. The Store command saves the current list to a file with the specified
name. The Load and Store commands allow you to create nested lists.
programs that can be navigated using the directive
{$PRG:Directives}.

The Modify command brings up the {Modify program:NewProg} dialog box,
in which you can change the program name, path, command line,
launch options, and also reassign the program call key.

The New command brings up the {New program:NewProg} dialog box,
which allows you to add a new program to the Programs list.

The Icon command allows you to create a file to run the selected program.
using {"icons":ULoadIcon}. After selecting the file name (.PRG) in the dialog
In the {Create a program icon:FileDialog} window, the "icon" will automatically open
behind the current dialog box.

The Edit command allows you to edit a file created by the Icon command.
After selecting the file name (.PRG) in the dialog box
{Edit a program icon:FileDialog} dialog box appears
{Modify program:NewProg} (see above).

The Delete command removes a program from the Programs list.

The {Adjust:NewItemPos} command allows you to move an item to a different location.
on the list.

.topic NewProg
{ New program / Modify program :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The New program / Modify program dialog box contains:

  lines input
(Program title, Program path,
Command line, Filename mask,
Line num mask, Source, Result)
  switches (Main)
  switches (Setup)
  switches (Options)
  Hot key selector and Hot keys button
  OK, Cancel buttons

The Program title input line contains the name of the program.

The Program path input line contains the name of the program or directive

{$ARC:Directives} {$DBASE:Directives} {$EDIT:Directives} {$HELP:Directives}
{$HTML:Directives} {$ICON:Directives} {$PANEL:Directives} {$SAMEWIN:Directives}
{$VIEW:Directives} {$XEDIT:Directives} {$XNT:Directives} {$XVIEW:Directives}
{$XW:Directives} {$XX:Directives}

The Command line input line may contain a command line,
passed to the program being launched. Directives can be used

{$CLIP:Directives} {$CMD:Directives} {$CN:Directives} {$CURDIR:Directives}
{$DAY:Directives} {$DIRARC:Directives} {$DIRNAME:Directives} {$ENV:Directives}
{$EXT:Directives} {$FILTER:Directives} {$FIND1ST:Directives} {$FINDDIR:Directives}
{$FINDNAME:Directives} {$FNAME:Directives} {$FYEAR:Directives} {$GET:Directives}
{$HIST:Directives} {$HOUR:Directives} {$HREF:Directives} {$KBD:Directives}
{$LEFT:Directives} {$MAC:Directives} {$MEM:Directives} {$MENU:Directives}
{$MIN:Directives} {$MONTH:Directives} {$MSEC:Directives} {$MSG:Directives}
{$NAME:Directives} {$NOMSGWIN:Directives} {$NOREDRAW:Directives} {$NOREREAD:Directives}
{$NTM:Directives} {$OEXT:Directives} {$ONAME:Directives} {$OPATH:Directives}
{$OPPOSITE:Directives} {$PATH:Directives} {$PRG:Directives} {$PRINT:Directives}
{$PROMPT:Directives} {$PUT:Directives} {$RDBLK:Directives} {$REPORT:Directives}
{$RIGHT: Directives} {$SEC:Directives} {$SEL:Directives} {$SET:Directives}
{$SLAPPEND:Directives} {$SLATTR:Directives} {$SLBKSLSH:Directives} {$SLDMASK:Directives}
{$SLPATH:Directives} {$SLPREFIX:Directives} {$SLQUOTES:Directives} {$SLSIZE:Directives}
{$SLSKIPD:Directives} {$SLSUFFIX:Directives} {$SLTIME:Directives} {$SLTMASK:Directives}
{$SWAPDIR:Directives} {$USERSCR:Directives} {$VM:Directives} {$WINCLIP:Directives}
{$WORD:Directives} {$WRBLK:Directives} {$XM:Directives} {$YEAR:Directives}

Input lines Filename mask, Line num mask can contain filters

{$COPY():FilterDirectives}, {$POS():FilterDirectives}, {$SEARCH():FilterDirectives}

and macros

{$DOWN():FilterDirectives}, {$UP():FilterDirectives},

allowing the {Message} window to determine the file name and line number from the text
(The Message switch must be on). For testing
To use the Filename mask and Line num mask filters, you can use the string
Source input, which specifies a sample line of source text,
In this case, the Result fields will display the result of the work of the specified
Filename mask and Line num mask filters (file name and line:column number)
in the original text).

If Swap mode is selected, the main program will attempt to swap out a large
part of its code in XMS (Extended memory) or in EMS (Expanded memory),
or, if neither is possible, to a file on disk.
{ATTENTION!!!:Color_4}
This mode cannot be used to execute resident programs.

If the Unload mode is selected, the main program will completely release
the memory it occupies, providing it to the program being launched,
However, the return process will take a little longer.
{ATTENTION!!!:Color_4}
This mode must be used to execute resident programs.

If the None mode is selected, then the program being launched
approximately as much memory as shown will be provided
free memory indicator in the lower right corner of the screen at the moment
execution time of the operation, plus the size of the overlay buffer.
{ATTENTION!!!:Color_4}
This mode cannot be used to run resident
programs.

If the Save editor files switch is enabled
( [X] ),
then before starting the program the command {Save all:FSaveAll} will be executed.
It is recommended to always enable it if Unload mode is selected; otherwise
In this case, the changes you made will remain unsaved.

If the Save desktop switch is enabled
( [X] ),
then the command will be executed before starting the program
{Save desktop:OSaveOptions}.

If the Load Snipper switch is enabled
( [X] ),
then the resident utility {Snipper} will be loaded before starting the program.

If the Message switch is on
( [X] ),
then the result of the running program will appear in the {Message} window.

If the Load COMMAND.COM switch is enabled
( [X] ),
then another copy of COMMAND.COM will be downloaded.

If the Swap to disk switch is enabled
( [X] ),
then the code will always be unloaded to disk (in order to
the program being launched could fully utilize EMS or XMS).

Using the {Hot key:KeyView} selector, you can set the following for this
hotkey programs for quick access. If you want
call a program by pressing several keys in sequence,
you need to use the Hot keys button, which opens a dialog box
window {Program hot key sequence:HotKeyListDlg}.

After entering the appropriate data, press Enter or the OK button.
The new program will appear in the Programs list of the dialog box.
{Program list:ProgList}.

The string entered in the Program arguments window is substituted for

launched from the {Program list:ProgList} dialog box or by
hotkey {Execute:UExecute}.

.topic UPhoneBook
{ UserｳPhone book (Alt+PgDn) :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Phone book command displays the {Phone list:PhoneBook} dialog box.

.topic PhoneBook
{ Phone list :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Phone list dialog box contains:

  list previously introduced phones
(Name Phone)
  buttons Dial, Modify, New, Delete,
Find, Adjust

Each list item, in addition to the name, number and notes, may contain
it contains the same list of phones as the one to which it belongs
(analogous to DOS directory).

The Dial command opens a {Terminal} window and inserts the selected number
to {autodial queue:Dialer}. If the Ctrl key is pressed,
The dialog box closes.

The Modify command brings up the {Modify phone entry:NewPhone} dialog box,
in which you can change the name, number or notes.

The New command displays the {New phone entry:NewPhone} dialog box,
which allows you to include a new element in the list.

The Delete command removes an item from the list.

The Find command allows you to find a substring specified in the {Find} dialog box.
(Ctrl+L - search for the next element).

The {Adjust:NewPhonePos} command allows you to move an element to another
list-"catalog".

The Import command (F4) allows you to insert the described file into the current "directory"
in the selected text file, the structure looks like this:

NAME Subname\Name
PHONE 123-4567
NOTES No notes

* * * * * * *

NAME Subname\Name
PHONE 987-6543
NOTES No notes

The words NAME, PHONE, NOTES are key and must be present.
in a text file.

The Export command (F5) allows you to create a text file with the structure
current "directory" in the format described above.

The Abort command (F6) interrupts the auto-dial process.

Pressing Ctrl+W opens
{directory history window:PromptHistory}.

.topic NewPhone
{ New phone entry / Modify phone entry :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The New phone entry / Modify phone entry dialog box contains
input lines Name, Phone and Notes, in which you indicate your name,
phone number and explanations for it. If the Phone line begins
with the '>' symbol (ASCII 62), then {Dial prefix:ModemSetup} and
{Dial suffix:ModemSetup} are not sent, but all necessary commands
must be present in this line, for example:

>ats37=6dp123456|

.topic UDecoders
{ UserｳDecoders (Ctrl+F6) :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Decoders team provides a convenient mechanism for recoding
text in windows of the following types:

{text editors:ASCIIEditor};
{text viewer window:TextViewer};
{windows for viewing .DBF files:DataViewer};
{HTML file viewer windows:HTMLViewer};
{terminal window:Terminal};
{File Manager:Panel window}.

If the active window on the screen is a window of one of the above
types and a user-defined list of transcoders contains
one or more elements when running the Decoders command (Ctrl+F6)
a menu for selecting a transcoder will appear on the screen; otherwise
The {User defined decoder list:DecoderList} dialog box will open.

.topic DecoderList
The User defined decoder list dialog box is designed to create
own list of recoders (XLAT tables), allowing
Easily perform text encoding in the following types of windows:

{text editors:ASCIIEditor};
{text viewer window:TextViewer};
{windows for viewing .DBF files:DataViewer};
{HTML file viewer windows:HTMLViewer};
{terminal window:Terminal};
{File Manager:Panel window}.

The window contains a user-created list of Decoders and buttons
Apply, Modify, New, Delete, Move up/down (hot keys)
Ctrl+Up/Ctrl+Down).

See also {UserｳDecoders:UDecoders}

.topicDecoderListItem
In the Decoder title input line, enter a title for this
transcoder.

In the input lines In XLAT file and Out XLAT file, specify the file names,
which stores tables for converting input symbols
(applies to all types of windows) and exit (applies only to
{text editor windows:ASCIIEditor},
{windows for viewing .DBF files:DataViewer} and
{terminal windows:Terminal}) threads. The table is an array
characters of 256 bytes in size.

.topic SelectDecoder
Select the menu item to recode the text in the current window.

.topic ResetDecoder
The Reset command cancels the conversion and returns the text in the current window.
to its original state.

.topic FileManager
The File Manager command opens the {File Manager:Panel} window, which allows you to
perform various operations with files and directories.

.topic Panel,AltPanel,CtrlPanel,ArcPanel
{ File Manager :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The File Manager window is a file processor similar to
popular shell program The Norton Commander and has
advanced capabilities for performing various operations with files and
catalogues, as well as archives.

The window contains two panels - left and right, as well as a line
input {Prompt:PromptLine}. The transition from one panel to another is carried out
using the Tab keys or Ctrl+Left and Ctrl+Right, from the panel to the Prompt line and
back - using the keys Ctrl+Down and Ctrl+Up.

To sequentially search for files (directories) by letters of the name
Press Alt+S and then press the keys corresponding to the letters
file or directory name. See also
{OptionsｳFile ManagerｳIncremental search options:OFMOptions}.

To quickly navigate to the desired directory, you can use the window
{directory history:PromptHistory}, which opens when
by pressing the keys Ctrl+W.

The {command history:PromptHistory} window that appears when you press keys
Ctrl+Q allows you to quickly select and place in the Prompt line
one of the previously entered commands.

The File Manager window menu is called by right-clicking or by pressing
Alt+F10 keys.

The size of panels and the entire window can be changed using the {Resize/move:WResize} command.
(Ctrl+F5) or by clicking with the mouse on any corner of the window frame or the lower middle
framework.

File Manager window commands:

.topic FMMiscHotkeys
Hot keys for the {File Manager:Panel} window:

Alt+G Change sort index and color of the selected file
or a group of files
Alt+? Place the full name of the selected file in the Prompt line
Alt+GrayPlus Select all files with the same name as the current one
Alt+GrayMinus Deselect all files with the same name as the current one
Alt+F4 Close the File Manager window

Ctrl+L {Info} mode for opposite panel
Ctrl+@ {Quick view:QuickView} mode for the opposite panel
Ctrl+Space {Description:QuickDescr} mode for the opposite panel
Ctrl+? Place the name of the left panel directory in the Prompt line
Ctrl+? Place the name of the right panel directory in the Prompt line
Ctrl+Del Delete the selected file or group of files from the panel list
Ctrl+Up Exit {file list view mode:ReadFileList} and from the archive
Ctrl+Down Go to the input line {Prompt:PromptLine}
Ctrl+GrayPlus Select all files with the same extension as the current one
Ctrl+GrayMinus Deselect all files with the same extension as the current one
Ctrl+F3 Open the current file in {Hex viewer window:HexViewer}
Ctrl+F4 Open the current file in the {Hex editor:HexEditor} window
Ctrl+F5 Copy only the current file (directory) regardless of
discharge
Ctrl+F6 Rename only the current file (directory) regardless of
discharge
Ctrl+F8 Delete only the current file (directory) regardless of
discharge

Shift+Space Select all files and all directories
Shift+GrayPlus Select all files with the same color as the current one
Shift+F2 Open the description file in {text editor window:ASCIIEditor}
Shift+F4 Command {FileｳOpen:FOpen}
Shift+F11 Toggle sorting mode for selected files

Ctrl+Shift+B Brief mode with long names
Ctrl+Shift+F {Full} mode with long names
Ctrl+Shift+N Open the {Advanced panel filter:AdvancedFilter} dialog box

.topic FMCopyOptions
{ File copy/rename options :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
In the File copy/rename options dialog box you can change the settings
{File Manager:Panel} windows used when performing operations
copying and renaming files.

The File exists action radio buttons allow you to choose one of four
options in case when copying or renaming a file
There is already a file with the same name on the disk:

  Prompt -
choosing further actions with the help of
{confirmation windows:CopySkipDialog};
  Overwrite all -
overwrite all existing files;
  Skip all -
skip all existing files;
  Compare by time/size -
compare time and file size
and act depending on the state
File compare action switches (see below).

The File compare action switches allow you to set different
actions for each of the possible results of comparison over time
and the size of the copied and existing files:

  Newer and longer -
the file being copied is newer and larger,
than the existing one;
  Newer and shorter -
the file being copied is newer and smaller,
than the existing one;
  Newer and same size -
the file being copied is newer,
than the existing one,
but their sizes are the same;
  Older and longer -
the file being copied is older and larger,
than the existing one;
  Older and shorter -
the file being copied is older and smaller,
than the existing one;
  Older and same size -
the file being copied is older,
than the existing one,
but their sizes are the same;
  Same time, longer -
the file being copied is larger,
than the existing one,
but their time coincides;
  Same time, shorter -
the file being copied is smaller,
than the existing one,
but their time coincides;
  Same time and size -
The files are identical in time and size.

Each of the File compare action switches can take any value.
of six states:

[?] - {Prompt:CopySkipDialog}
[O] - Overwrite
[A] - Append
[R] - Resume
[N] - New
[S] - Skip

Thus, depending on the result of the comparison of time and size
files and switch states can be automatically performed
this or that action.

Options Check free disk space before Copy and Copy/rename descriptions
duplicate the corresponding options specified in the window
{File Manager options:OFMOptions}.

If the Clear ReadOnly attribute on Copy flag is enabled,
When copying files, the ReadOnly attribute is removed, which may turn out to be
convenient if the files to be copied are on a CD-ROM disk.

If the Unselect skipped files flag is enabled, the files that are skipped when
were missed during group copying or renaming,
The selection in the {File Manager:Panel} window panel is removed.

If the Hide Copy progress window flag is enabled, when copying
files, a window with a slider displaying the process will not appear
copying. The information will still be displayed in the status bar.

If the Hide Copy statistics window flag is enabled, when copying
files, the window displaying group statistics will not appear
copying.

If the Enable recursive Copy/Move flag is enabled, you can copy
or move a directory to a child subdirectory.

If the Do not copy/move empty dirs flag is enabled, the program will not
copy or move empty directories.

Restore settings switches on completing the Copy/Rename operation
allow you to restore previous settings after the end of the current one
copy or move file operations, making current settings
disposable:

[ ] Settings in this dialog box -
settings in this dialog box;

[ ] Modified File Manager options -
duplicate window settings
{File Manager options:OFMOptions}.

.topic CopyDialog
{Copy (F5) :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
Below are the different options for executing the Copy command.
in the {File Manager:Panel} window.

1.
 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Copy ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ {Copy "text.doc" to:AbsColor_$3f} ｺ
 ｺ { E ? \DOC\ :AbsColor_$1f} { :AbsColor_$20} ｺ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ { OK :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ { Cancel :AbsColor_$50} ﾜ  ｺ
 ｺ    ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ            ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ  ｺ
 ﾈﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｼ
The file "text.doc" from the current directory will be copied to the file
E:\DOC\text.doc (if there is no DOC directory on drive E:, it will be created).

2.
 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Copy ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ {Copy "text.doc" to:AbsColor_$3f} ｺ
 ｺ { E ? \DOC :AbsColor_$1f} { :AbsColor_$20} ｺ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ { OK :AbsColor_$5f} ﾜ { Cancel :AbsColor_$50} ﾜ  ｺ
 ｺ    ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ            ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ  ｺ
 ﾈﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｼ
If there is a DOC directory on the E: drive, the "text.doc" file from the current directory
will be copied to the file E:\DOC\text.doc; otherwise, to the file E:\doc.

3.
 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Copy ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ {Copy "text.doc" to:AbsColor_$3f} ｺ
 ｺ { E ? \DOC\*.txt :AbsColor_$1f} { :AbsColor_$20} ｺ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ { OK :AbsColor_$5f} ﾜ { Cancel :AbsColor_$50} ﾜ  ｺ
 ｺ    ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ            ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ  ｺ
 ﾈﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｼ
The file "text.doc" from the current directory will be copied to the file
E:\DOC\text.txt (if there is no DOC directory on drive E:, it will be created).

4.
 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Copy ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ {Copy xxx selected files to:AbsColor_$3f} ｺ
 ｺ { E ? \DOC\*.txt :AbsColor_$1f} { :AbsColor_$20} ｺ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ { OK :AbsColor_$5f} ﾜ { Cancel :AbsColor_$50} ﾜ  ｺ
 ｺ    ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ            ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ  ｺ
 ﾈﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｼ
All selected files from the current directory will be copied to files
E:\DOC\*.txt (if there is no DOC directory on drive E:, it will be created).

5.
 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Copy ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ {Copy xxx selected files to:AbsColor_$3f} ｺ
 ｺ { +E ? \DOC\alldocs.txt :AbsColor_$1f} { :AbsColor_$20} ｺ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ { OK :AbsColor_$5f} ﾜ { Cancel :AbsColor_$50} ﾜ  ｺ
 ｺ    ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ            ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ  ｺ
 ﾈﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｼ
If the destination name is preceded by '+', all selected files from the current
directory will be copied to the file E:\DOC\alldocs.txt by the append method
Append (if there is no DOC directory on drive E:, it will be created).

6.
 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Copy ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ {Copy the directory "TXT" to:AbsColor_$3f} ｺ
 ｺ { E ? \DOC\ :AbsColor_$1f} { :AbsColor_$20} ｺ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ Filter { *.doc:AbsColor_$1f} New mask { *.txt:AbsColor_$1f} ｺ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ { OK :AbsColor_$5f} ﾜ { Cancel :AbsColor_$50} ﾜ  ｺ
 ｺ    ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ            ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ  ｺ

(if any) will be copied to files E:\DOC\TXT\...\*.txt
preserving the structure of subdirectories (if there are no corresponding ones on drive E:
directories, then they will be created).

 ﾈﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｼ

10. Working with archives:
 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Copy ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ

12. Copying to multiple files (file split)
 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Copy ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ {Copy "text.doc" to:AbsColor_$3f} ｺ
 ｺ { /100K E ? \DOC\*.%03dtxt :AbsColor_$1f} { :AbsColor_$20} ｺ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ { OK :AbsColor_$5f} ﾜ { Cancel :AbsColor_$50} ﾜ  ｺ
 ｺ    ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ            ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ  ｺ
 ﾈﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｼ
The file "text.doc" from the current directory will be copied into several files
E:\DOC\text.nnntxt (if there is no DOC directory on drive E:, it will be created).
The number of files is determined by the size of the source file and the specified size
(for example, 100 kilobytes). The destination string can contain a specifier
formatting (e.g. %03d) to form the name of each resulting
file by its serial number. If the specifier is not specified, the created
The files will have extensions determined by their ordinal number.

13. Copying with optimal filling
 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Copy ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ {Copy xxx selected files to:AbsColor_$3f} ｺ
 ｺ { /100K E ? \DOC\DOC%03d\ :AbsColor_$1f} { :AbsColor_$20} ｺ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ { OK :AbsColor_$5f} ﾜ { Cancel :AbsColor_$50} ﾜ  ｺ
 ｺ    ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ            ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ  ｺ
 ﾈﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｼ
All selected files from the current directory will be copied to the directories
E:\DOC\DOCnnn so that in each directory the total size
files did not exceed the specified value and was, if possible,
close to him.

14. Copying with {regular expressions:RegExp}
 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Copy ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ
 ｺ                                              ｺ
 ｺ {Copy xxx selected files to :AbsColor_$3f} ｺ
 ｺ { >(.*)( )(\(track..\))(.mp3)>\2\1\0\3 :AbsColor_$1f} { :AbsColor_$20} ｺ
 ｺ                                              ｺ
 ｺ { OK :AbsColor_$5f} ﾜ { Cancel :AbsColor_$50} ﾜ  ｺ
 ｺ   ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ                         ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ  ｺ
 ﾈﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｼ
If the specified destination string begins with the '>' character, the program
treats this string as a regular expression consisting of two
parts separated by another '>' symbol and applies this expression
to find and perform a copy operation on a file or group of files.
In this case, all selected files whose names match the first
parts of the regular expression {(.*)( )(\(track..\))(.mp3):Color_2}, for example:

{One song (track01).mp3:Color_2}
{Another song (track02).mp3:Color_2}

will be copied accordingly to

{(track01) One song.mp3:Color_2}
{(track02) Another song.mp3:Color_2}

according to the rules of substitution of groups of strings defined by the second part of the regular
expressions {\2\1\0\3:Color_2} (see also {Replace}).

If the second part of the regular expression starts with a directory name, for example:

{>(.*)( )(\(track..\))(.mp3)>C?\\MP3_NEW\\\2\1\0\3:Color_2}

The resulting file will be created in the specified directory.

15. Group copying with confirmation
 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Copy ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ {Copy xxx selected files to:AbsColor_$3f} ｺ
 ｺ { ?E ? \DOC\*.txt :AbsColor_$1f} { :AbsColor_$20} ｺ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ { OK :AbsColor_$5f} ﾜ { Cancel :AbsColor_$50} ﾜ  ｺ
 ｺ    ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ            ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ  ｺ
 ﾈﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｼ
If the specified destination string begins with the character '?',
A dialog box will appear before each file is copied.
to confirm the operation.

See also {SysCopy:NT_SysCopy}

windows {Clipboard}.

7. Copying using {regular expressions:RegExp}
 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Copy ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ
 ｺ                                              ｺ
 ｺ {Copy :AbsColor_$3f} ｺ
 ｺ { C ? \MP3\*.mp3 :AbsColor_$1f} { :AbsColor_$20} ｺ
 ｺ {to:AbsColor_$3f} ｺ
 ｺ { >(.*)( )(\(track..\))(.mp3)>\2\1\0\3 :AbsColor_$1f} { :AbsColor_$20} ｺ
 ｺ                                              ｺ
 ｺ { OK :AbsColor_$5f} ﾜ { Cancel :AbsColor_$50} ﾜ  ｺ
 ｺ    ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ                        ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ  ｺ
 ﾈﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｼ
If the specified destination string begins with the '>' character, the program
treats this string as a regular expression consisting of two
parts separated by another '>' symbol and applies this expression
to find and perform a copy operation on a file or group of files.
In this case, all files in the C:\MP3 directory whose names match
the first part of the regular expression {(.*)( )(\(track..\))(.mp3):Color_2},
For example:

{One song (track01).mp3:Color_2}
{Another song (track02).mp3:Color_2}

will be copied accordingly to

{(track01) One song.mp3:Color_2}
{(track02) Another song.mp3:Color_2}

according to the rules of substitution of groups of strings defined by the second part of the regular
expressions {\2\1\0\3:Color_2} (see also {Replace}).

If the second part of the regular expression starts with a directory name, for example:

{>(.*)( )(\(track..\))(.mp3)>C?\\MP3_NEW\\\2\1\0\3:Color_2}

The resulting file will be created in the specified directory.

8. Group copying with confirmation
 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Copy ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ {Copy:AbsColor_$3f} ｺ
 ｺ { *.doc :AbsColor_$1f} { :AbsColor_$20} ｺ
 ｺ {to:AbsColor_$3f} ｺ
 ｺ { ?E ? \DOC\ :AbsColor_$1f} { :AbsColor_$20} ｺ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ { OK :AbsColor_$5f} ﾜ { Cancel :AbsColor_$50} ﾜ  ｺ
 ｺ    ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ            ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ  ｺ
 ﾈﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｼ
If the specified destination string begins with the character '?',
A dialog box will appear before each file is copied.
to confirm the operation.

See also {SysCopy:NT_SysCopy}

.topic ArcCopyDlg
The Copy/move to archive command (Shift+F1) opens a dialog box,
in which you can select the desired archiving method for the selected
in the current panel of the {File Manager:Panel} window of files or directories.

The Copy/move to archive dialog box consists of the following elements:

  Line input Destination
When copying a single file or directory, this line initially contains
the name of this file/directory without the extension. When copying multiple
selected files or directories line contains the name of the current directory
panel. You can change the contents of this line if the archive
The file must be named differently.

  Lines Enter Packer name, Command line, Prefix
  Exec options switches
These elements contain data stored in files.
{archiver settings:Archivers}, for the Archivers selected in the list
archiver. When moving through the Archivers list, the values of these
elements are changed. You can modify these if necessary.
values.

  Line Enter Password
If the Prefix line is not empty, you can specify a password in the Password line.
archiving.

  Copy or move switch
If the Delete source files flag is set, the archiver will perform the operation
Move instead of Add.

  Empty dirs switch ( when There is highlighted catalogs )
If the Skip flag is set, empty directories will not be included in the archive file.

  List existing Archivers?
You can navigate the list using the Up and Down keys even if
other dialog elements (except switches) are active.
You can also open the history window for input lines by pressing Shift+Down.
By pressing Ctrl+Enter, Space or by double-clicking on
When you press the mouse button, a dialog box appears for editing the settings.
selected archiver.

See also:

{Copy to archive:CopyDialog}
{Move to archive:RenMovDialog}

 ｺ    ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ            ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ  ｺ

The file "text.doc" from the current directory will be moved to the file
E:\DOC\text.txt (if there is no DOC directory on drive E:, it will be created).
(Assuming E: is not the current drive.)

3.
 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Rename/Move ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ

All selected files from the current directory will be moved to files
E:\DOC\*.txt (if there is no DOC directory on drive E:, it will be created).

4.
 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Rename/Move ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ

Append (if there is no DOC directory on drive E:, it will be created).

11. Working with archives:
 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Rename/Move ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ
 ｺ                                      ｺ
 ｺ {Rename or move xxx selected files to:AbsColor_$3f} ｺ
 ｺ { ARJ ? E ? \DOC\DOCS.ARJ :AbsColor_$1f} { :AbsColor_$20} ｺ
 ｺ                                      ｺ
 ｺ { OK :AbsColor_$5f} ﾜ { Cancel :AbsColor_$50} ﾜ  ｺ
 ｺ   ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ                 ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ  ｺ
 ﾈﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｼ
All selected files from the current directory will be packed with the ARJ archiver.
into the file E:\DOC\DOCS.ARJ, and then deleted by it.
(see also {Copy/move to archive dialog:ArcCopyDlg}).

12. Moving to multiple files (file split)
 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Rename/Move ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ {Rename or move "text.doc" to:AbsColor_$3f} ｺ
 ｺ { /100K E ? \DOC\*.%03dtxt :AbsColor_$1f} { :AbsColor_$20} ｺ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ { OK :AbsColor_$5f} ﾜ { Cancel :AbsColor_$50} ﾜ  ｺ
 ｺ    ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ            ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ  ｺ
 ﾈﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｼ
The file "text.doc" from the current directory will be moved into several files
E:\DOC\text.nnntxt (if there is no DOC directory on drive E:, it will be created).
The number of files is determined by the size of the source file and the specified size
(for example, 100 kilobytes). You can specify a specifier in the destination string
formatting (e.g. %03d) to form the name of each resulting
file by its serial number. If the specifier is not specified, the created
The files will have extensions determined by their ordinal number.
{Note:Color_5} movement within one disk occurs by
cutting off the next portion of the file from the end of the original file and simultaneously
reducing the size of the original file, so to perform this operation
the amount of free disk space required is no more than the specified size of one
the resulting file, and in the case where the file is split into two pieces,
there must be free space no larger than the size of the last portion,
which may be significantly less than specified.

13. Moving with optimal filling
 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Rename/Move ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ
 ｺ                                      ｺ
 ｺ {Rename or move xxx selected files to:AbsColor_$3f} ｺ
 ｺ { /100K E ? \DOC\DOC%03d\ :AbsColor_$1f} { :AbsColor_$20} ｺ
 ｺ                                      ｺ
 ｺ { OK :AbsColor_$5f} ﾜ { Cancel :AbsColor_$50} ﾜ  ｺ
 ｺ   ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ                 ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ  ｺ
 ﾈﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｼ
All selected files from the current directory will be moved to the directories
E:\DOC\DOCnnn so that in each directory the total size
files did not exceed the specified value and was, if possible,
close to him.

14. Renaming with {regular expressions:RegExp}
 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Rename/Move ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ
 ｺ                                              ｺ
 ｺ {Rename or move xxx selected files to :AbsColor_$3f} ｺ
 ｺ { >(.*)( )(\(track..\))(.mp3)>\2\1\0\3 :AbsColor_$1f} { :AbsColor_$20} ｺ
 ｺ                                              ｺ
 ｺ { OK :AbsColor_$5f} ﾜ { Cancel :AbsColor_$50} ﾜ  ｺ
 ｺ   ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ                         ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ  ｺ
 ﾈﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｼ
If the specified destination string begins with the '>' character, the program
treats this string as a regular expression consisting of two
parts separated by another '>' symbol and applies this expression
to find and perform a rename operation on a file or group of files.
In this case, all selected files whose names match the first
parts of the regular expression {(.*)( )(\(track..\))(.mp3):Color_2}, for example:

{One song (track01).mp3:Color_2}
{Another song (track02).mp3:Color_2}

will be renamed accordingly to

{(track01) One song.mp3:Color_2}
{(track02) Another song.mp3:Color_2}

according to the rules of substitution of groups of strings defined by the second part of the regular
expressions {\2\1\0\3:Color_2} (see also {Replace}).

If the second part of the regular expression starts with a directory name, for example:

{>(.*)( )(\(track..\))(.mp3)>C?\\MP3_NEW\\\2\1\0\3:Color_2}

The resulting file will be created in the specified directory.

15. Group renaming with confirmation
 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Rename/Move ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ
 ｺ                                      ｺ
 ｺ {Rename or move xxx selected files to:AbsColor_$3f} ｺ
 ｺ { ?E ? \DOC\*.txt :AbsColor_$1f} { :AbsColor_$20} ｺ
 ｺ                                      ｺ
 ｺ { OK :AbsColor_$5f} ﾜ { Cancel :AbsColor_$50} ﾜ  ｺ
 ｺ    ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ                ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ  ｺ
 ﾈﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｼ
If the specified destination string begins with the character '?',
Before renaming each file, a dialog box will appear
to confirm the operation.

See also {SysCopy:NT_SysCopy}

.topic ShiftRenMovDialog
{ Shift+RenMov (Shift+F6) :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
Below are the different options for executing the Shift+RenMov command.
in the {File Manager:Panel} window.

1.
 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Rename/Move ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ

 ｺ { *.txt :AbsColor_$1f} { :AbsColor_$20} ｺ
 ｺ                                  ｺ

 ｺ    ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ            ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ  ｺ
 ﾈﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｼ
The file "text.doc" from the current directory will be renamed to the file text.txt.

2.
 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Rename/Move ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ

 ｺ {to:AbsColor_$3f} ｺ
 ｺ { E ? \DOC :AbsColor_$1f} { :AbsColor_$20} ｺ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ { OK :AbsColor_$5f} ﾜ { Cancel :AbsColor_$50} ﾜ  ｺ
 ｺ    ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ            ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ  ｺ
 ﾈﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｼ
All files with the .doc extension from the C:\DOC directory and all subdirectories
(if any) will be moved to the E:\DOC directory without saving
subdirectory structures (if there is no DOC directory on the E: drive, it will be
created).

3.
 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Rename/Move ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ {Rename or move:AbsColor_$3f} ｺ

 ｺ {to:AbsColor_$3f} ｺ
 ｺ { E ? \DOC :AbsColor_$1f} { :AbsColor_$20} ｺ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ { OK :AbsColor_$5f} ﾜ { Cancel :AbsColor_$50} ﾜ  ｺ
 ｺ    ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ            ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ  ｺ
 ﾈﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｼ
All files with the .doc extension on the current drive will be moved to
directory E:\DOC without preserving the subdirectory structure
(if there is no DOC directory on drive E:, it will be created).

4.
 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Rename/Move ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ

 ｺ {DOC :AbsColor_$1f} { :AbsColor_$20} ｺ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ { OK :AbsColor_$5f} ﾜ { Cancel :AbsColor_$50} ﾜ  ｺ
 ｺ    ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ            ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ  ｺ

all files and directories whose names are stored in the selected text
windows {Clipboard}.

7. Renaming with {regular expressions:RegExp}
 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Rename/Move ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ
 ｺ                                              ｺ
 ｺ {Rename or move :AbsColor_$3f} ｺ
 ｺ { C ? \MP3\*.mp3 :AbsColor_$1f} { :AbsColor_$20} ｺ
 ｺ {to:AbsColor_$3f} ｺ
 ｺ { >(.*)( )(\(track..\))(.mp3)>\2\1\0\3 :AbsColor_$1f} { :AbsColor_$20} ｺ
 ｺ                                              ｺ
 ｺ { OK :AbsColor_$5f} ﾜ { Cancel :AbsColor_$50} ﾜ  ｺ
 ｺ    ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ                        ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ  ｺ
 ﾈﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｼ
If the specified destination string begins with the '>' character, the program
treats this string as a regular expression consisting of two
parts separated by another '>' symbol and applies this expression
to find and perform a rename operation on a file or group of files.
In this case, all files in the C:\MP3 directory whose names match
the first part of the regular expression {(.*)( )(\(track..\))(.mp3):Color_2},
For example:

{One song (track01).mp3:Color_2}
{Another song (track02).mp3:Color_2}

will be renamed accordingly to

{(track01) One song.mp3:Color_2}
{(track02) Another song.mp3:Color_2}

according to the rules of substitution of groups of strings defined by the second part of the regular
expressions {\2\1\0\3:Color_2} (see also {Replace}).

If the second part of the regular expression starts with a directory name, for example:

{>(.*)( )(\(track..\))(.mp3)>C?\\MP3_NEW\\\2\1\0\3:Color_2}

The resulting file will be created in the specified directory.

 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Rename/Move ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ {Rename or move:AbsColor_$3f} ｺ
 ｺ { *.doc :AbsColor_$1f} { :AbsColor_$20} ｺ
 ｺ {to:AbsColor_$3f} ｺ
 ｺ { ?E ? \DOC :AbsColor_$1f} { :AbsColor_$20} ｺ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ { OK :AbsColor_$5f} ﾜ { Cancel :AbsColor_$50} ﾜ  ｺ
 ｺ    ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ            ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ  ｺ
 ﾈﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｼ
If the specified destination string begins with the character '?',
Before renaming each file, a dialog box will appear
to confirm the operation.

 ﾉﾍ [  ] ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍ Delete ﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｻ
 ｺ                                  ｺ
 ｺ {Delete:AbsColor_$3f} ｺ

 ｺ    ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ            ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ  ｺ
 ﾈﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍﾍｼ

.topic DirSizes
{ Directory information :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
This window displays information for the selected directory:

Directory: Directory name
Files: Number of files and their total size
Total size: Total disk space taken up, taking into account cluster size.
Size on disk: Size on disk including compressed files (NTFS)
Subdirs: Number of subdirectories

Selected: The number of selected files and their total size
Total size: The total disk size of the selected files.
Size on disk: Size on disk including compressed allocated files (NTFS)

Free space: Free space on the current disk

The number of files and their total size are calculated for the selected
directory and all subdirectories.

Size on disk values are only displayed {when running under Windows NT:CN_NT}.

.topic FindFile
{ Find file :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Find file command displays the {Find file:FindFileDlg} dialog box,
allowing you to search for files on the disk by name.

.topic FindFileDlg
{ Find file :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Find file dialog box allows you to find files on your disk by name,
and also copy, move and delete found files.
You can use masks in the File(s) to find input line, for example:

*.TXT; C:\*.LH?; A:\*.BAT

or, if the UNIX style mask flag is set, masks in the form
{UNIX style wildcard:UnixWildcard}, for example:

*SS.[^EF]*

(all files with a name ending with letters
'SS', and with an extension starting with any
letters other than 'E' and 'F').

In addition, you can search for files whose size and/or creation time
satisfies the condition written in the form:

*.* > 65536 > 10-01-93 < 09:30

(Find all files on the current disk that are larger than 64 kB, created
after October 1, 1993 until half past nine in the morning).

You can also specify rough search criteria:

*.* | 64K | 10-02-93 | 09:30

(Find all files on the current disk that are approximately 64 kB in size
(65536-6554..65536+6554), created on October 1..3, 1993 between 09:20 and
(09:40 am).

Only signs are allowed to be used

< > = |

If the File(s) to find input line is empty, but there is a selection in the window
{Clipboard} text with file names or masks, the search will be performed
for all selected names (masks). Text in lines after the first space
ignored. For example, text selected in the Clipboard window may be
next:

SOMEFILE.TXT Some useful documentation
D:\*.DOC;D:\*.CHI;D:\*.LST;E:\*.*>256K
README.1ST;README.PLS Files to read

In the Containing text input line you can specify a keyword for search
in the file.

The Case sensitive flag specifies that uppercase and lowercase letters should be distinguished.

The Whole words only flag specifies that only whole words should be searched.

The Inverse flag specifies that files that do not contain the specified text should be searched for.

The {Regular expression:RegExp} flag specifies that the search text contains
specifiers similar to those used in the GREP program.

The XLAT flag allows searching for the specified text in encodings,
defined by the list {Decoders:DecoderList}.

The Search command starts searching for the specified files.

The Go to command closes the Find file dialog box and sets the cursor
active panel of the {File Manager:Panel} window on the selected file.

The Panel command writes the names of found files to the SELECTED.LST file.
and opens the active panel in the {Read file list:ReadFileList} mode
to view the resulting text file.

The Clear command clears the list of found files.

The Drives command allows you to specify a list of drives on which the
a search will be carried out.

The Options command displays the {Find file options:FindFileOptions} dialog box,
where you can select the search area and set attributes for the search
files.

.topic FindFileOptions
In the Find file options dialog box, you can set file search options.

The Start from current directory flag specifies that the search should begin.
from the current directory.

The Scan subdirectories flag specifies that all subdirectories should be searched recursively.
subdirectories.

The Scan selected directories only flag specifies that the search should be recursive.
only in the selected directories; in this case, the Scan subdirectories flag must be
be installed.

The Search in archives flag specifies that all or
files matching the mask in the Archive name filter line as archives.

The Tagged files only flag specifies that the found files should be
in the list of selected files
(see also {OptionsｳFile ManagerｳSave directory selection:OFMOptions}).

The Select found files flag indicates that the found files should be immediately
select for subsequent group operations {Copy:CopyDialog},
{Rename / Move:RenMovDialog}, {Delete:ShiftDeleteDialog} or for
opening found files in {Text viewer:TextViewer} windows,
{dBASE viewer:DataViewer}, {HTML viewer:HTMLViewer} (F3),
{Hex viewer:HexViewer} (Ctrl+F3), {Text editor:ASCIIEditor} (F4) or
{Hex editor:HexEditor} (Ctrl+F4). If the Tagged files only flag is enabled,
found files will be selected regardless of the flag state
Select found files.

The File attributes switches allow you to set file attributes,
by which the search will be carried out.

In the Archive name filter line, you can specify one or more masks.
names of files that will be considered archives when searching with the option enabled
Search in archives flag, for example, *.ZIP; *.ARJ; *.RAR
(see also {Setting file name masks for Advanced filter:AdvancedFilter}).
If this line is empty, the search will be performed across all files.

The Save/Restore Find file options and search drives flag allows
remember and restore the next time the program is launched
all file search settings.

When the Clear <Containing text> flag is enabled, input line data on open
input line Containing text when opening a dialog box
{Find file:FindFileDlg} will be empty; otherwise it will be
contain a substring of the previous search.

.topic Sort
{ Sort and display :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Sort and display command (Ctrl+S) opens a dialog box.
Panel sort and display options, where you can set the order
placing files in a window depending on the name (Name), extension
(Extension), creation time (Time), size (Size), ordinal
number present in the name and extension (Digital number), or in
according to the location on the disk (Disk order). In addition, files
You can sort by their {descriptions:FilesBBS} in alphabetical order
(Description) or in the order of their location in the text file of descriptors
(Description order). Case sensitive sort flags allow comparison
names of files, directories and description lines with or without taking into account
register, and in the input line Description compare pos you can specify,
From what position to compare file description lines.

The Sort direction radio buttons allow you to set the sorting direction:
Ascending - ascending, Descending - descending.

The way files and directories are displayed relative to each other in the panel is determined
by setting the Sort priority: Directories first switches
directories, Files first - files first, Mixed - files and directories
mixed together.

The Selected first/last flag allows you to set the mode in which
Selected files or directories are automatically moved to the beginning (F)
or to the end of the list (L). This mode can also be switched
by pressing Shift+F11 in the panel.

File group options radio buttons allow you to enable or disable
highlighting and sorting file groups in the panel; the name mask,
The color and index of the group are set in the dialog box
{File group list:GroupDlg}, called by the Groups command in the dialog box
{File Manager options:OFMOptions} window. In the input line next to
The Sort by group index switch allows you to specify a list of group indices,
participating in the sorting, and their priority will be determined
in the order of listing, for example:

{ 10,9,20,50 :AbsColor_$1f}

Separators can be any non-numeric characters (space, comma,
semicolon, etc.).

Using the Win95/NT file time/size options switches, you can
in the DOS window of the Windows 95/NT operating system, select to display
and sort one of three times of files or directories:

  Last modification time - time last one modifications file
  Last access time - time last appeals To file
  File creation time - time creation file

and select the file size display mode
(only {when running under Windows NT:CN_NT} with the NTFS file system)

[ ] Size on disk - sizes of compressed files

The Sort action switches allow you to select the sorting mode: fast
Sort in memory or rereading the contents
panels (Re-read directory).

Inverse long/short switch in Sort by name/extension mode
allows you to sort files and directories by their long names or extensions,
when short ones are displayed in the panel, and vice versa.

Mixed char/numerical switch in Sort by name/extension mode
allows you to sort files and directories by name or extension,
containing letters and numbers mixed together.

The Sort by "name.ext" string switch allows you to sort files and
directories by lines consisting of a name, a period, and an extension.

.topic Filter
{ Filter :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The Filter command (Ctrl+N) opens the Filter dialog box,
in which you can set a mask for files when reading directories.
For example, if you set the mask *.TXT, then the window will show
only files with the .TXT extension (if they exist in the current directory).
The Advanced filter button is used to open a dialog box.
{Advanced panel filter:AdvancedFilter}.

.topic AdvancedFilter
{ Advanced panel filter :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
In the Advanced panel filter dialog box (Ctrl+Shift+N) you can set
criteria for selecting files to display in the window panel {File Manager:Panel},
and also to perform group file operations Copy and Rename/Move.
{Setting file name masks for Advanced filter:Color_X}
The Filter input line allows you to specify one or more masks.
file names separated by ";" or "," characters, for example:

*.PAS;*.INC,*.ASM;*.OBJ,*.TPU

{ATTENTION!!!:Color_4}
If there are spaces in the string, they are considered part of the mask.
(to support Win95 LFN).

The "|" (Pipe) symbol in the Filter input line is used to exclude groups of files.
If the file name matches at least one of the masks listed
After this symbol, such a file does not pass filtering, for example:

*.PA?;*.INC|TP*.*;AP*.*

(all files with an extension starting with the letters
'PA' or 'INC', except for files named,
starting with the letters 'TP' or 'AP')

or

|*.EXE;*.TPU

(all files except files with extensions
'EXE' and 'TPU').

If the UNIX style mask flag is set, you must enter the following in the Filter input line:
Specify a mask in the form {UNIX style wildcard:UnixWildcard}, for example:

*SS.[^EF]*

(all files with a name ending with letters
'SS', and with an extension starting with any
letters other than 'E' and 'F').

To activate the Advanced filter mode, the Filter input line must be
non-empty.

The File date, File time and File size input lines allow you to specify
lower and upper limits for the creation time and size of displayed files.
If any of these lines is empty, the selection by this criterion is not performed.
is produced.

The File attributes switches allow you to set file attributes,
by which the selection will be made. In addition, they allow you to manage
selection of catalogs, despite the fact that the Advanced panel filter settings
apply only to files. For example, if you turn off the switches
Directory and Any file, then only files will be shown in the panel
without directories. And vice versa, if you turn on the Directory switch and
If you disable all others, then only directories will be shown in the panel.

If the Do not apply to archives or file lists flag is enabled, the filter is not
will work in archive viewing mode and {lists:ReadFileList}.

If the Clear on completing the Copy/Rename operation flag is enabled,
upon completion of the current group file operation, all installations
Advanced filter will be cleaned (disposable filter).

The Clear command clears all settings and turns off Advanced filter mode.

The Load and Store commands allow you to read and write settings.
Advanced filter.

.topic Archivers
When you select any item from the Archivers submenu, a dialog box appears.
Archiver setup, where you can set command lines and launch options
the corresponding archiver when viewing archives in the window panels
{File Manager:Panel} and performing various operations with archives.
In the lines Add, Add with dirs, Move, Move with dirs you can use
directives {$CN:Directives}, {$SWAPDIR:Directives} for setting
temporary directory archiver.

See also

{User defined archivers:UserArchivers}
{Using the $XNT:NT_Exec directive}

.topic UserArchivers
The User defined archivers command allows you to configure the program to work
with any type of archives, provided that the archiver can output
list of files contained in the archive. In the dialog box
{Archiver setup:Archivers} you need to specify, among other things, the name mask and
extensions for archive recognition, for example, *.AIN (Name mask),
as well as a command to create a text file list (View command).
The command may contain the directive {$MSG(FilterName): Directives},
where FilterName is the name of the filter program used for translation
lines output by the archiver to the standard output device,
into the required format of the following type:

DOCUMENT.TXT 34987 05.21.95 12:54:08
DOC\NEW\PAPER.DOC 156711 05.21.95 14:36:22

There should be no spaces before the file name. In addition, in the command
lines, as well as in the Extract and Extract with dirs lines, you can
use special directives {$ARC:Color_2} and {$SRC:Color_2},
replaced respectively by the name of the viewed/created
archive and the name of the file on which the panel cursor is located, or a line,
consisting of the List character and the name of the list file being created
for the archiver to perform an operation on a group of files. Directive
{$FMT():Color_2} specifies the format of the lines placed in the file list for
working with List commands of archivers. Parameter {$FMT():Color_2}
there must be a {$FILE:Color_2} directive. By default, lines are created in
format {$FMT($FILE):Color_2}, but if, for example, the lines should
start with the character "\", then you need to write {$FMT(\$FILE):Color_2}.
If the List file is not created when executing the command, then the directive
{$FMT():Color_2} is replaced by the correspondingly expanded name of the current
file. In this case, {$SRC:Color_2} is equivalent to {$FMT($FILE):Color_2}.
The {$LST:Color_2} directive is replaced with the name of the file list obtained in
result of executing the View command. This name can be used
a filter program to obtain a list of files of the specified format.
The {$DIRARC:Color_2} directive substitutes the current path into the command line.
the archive being viewed (without the archive name).

See also {Using the $XNT:NT_Exec Directive}

.topic OpenArchive
The Open archive command (Alt+A) opens the window in the {File Manager:Panel} panel.
selected archive file for viewing and performing various operations
with its contents.

.topic ArcPassword
Enter the password for the archive you are viewing.

.topic ReadFileList
The Read file list command (Alt+V) displays in the {File Manager:Panel} window panel
a text file containing file names. If the file contains
full names, then the panel emulates the directory system specified in this
file, on the specified or current disk. When displaying those files from the list,
which were found on the disk, the actual sizes, date,
time and attributes, and the rest have zero size, date - 01-01-80,
time - 00:00:00 and the Archive attribute. With files displayed in this way
all file operations are possible if such files are actually present on
disk. Exit from this mode by pressing Ctrl+Up in any
place, or Ctrl+PgUp in the topmost displayed directory. If at the same time
hold down the Shift key, the panel cursor will be set to the same file
(directory) on which it stood in File list mode, provided that such
the file (directory) exists.

See also {Copy to list:CopyDialog}

.topic SaveFocusedName
The Write name to history command (Alt+H) remembers the name of a file or directory,
where the cursor is located. You can quickly return to this place later,
by selecting the recorded name from the list in the {history window:PromptHistory}, which
opens when you press Ctrl+W.

When Mini status mode is enabled, there are three lines less than when

.topic Unfold
The Unfold subdirectories command (Alt+B) toggles the mode in which
The panel displays files located in the subdirectories of the current
directory, and the subdirectories themselves are not shown ("file tree").
The program may run out of memory if there are too many attached files.
In this case, the following message will appear:

ﾚﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄｿ
ｳ Too many files. ｳ
ﾀﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾄﾙ

See also {OptionsｳFile ManagerｳClear the Unfold flag on dir change:OFMOptions}

.topic FilesBBS
The Show file descriptions command (Ctrl+P) enables or disables the display
information about each file in the panel in {Full} mode, stored in the file,
whose name (or several names separated by the ';' symbol) is specified in
{File Manager options:OFMOptions} dialog box
(default FILES.BBS) This is a text file consisting of file names and
comments, for example:

SOMEFILE.ARJ Magic C++ Tools
ANYFILE.ARJ Powerful BP Tools
* * * * * * *
MYFILE.ZIP TASM library to build
an integrated environment

There must be at least one space between the file name and
its description. Line breaks are allowed, provided that the broken line
The line starts with a space. There are spaces at the beginning of the line with the file name.
It shouldn't be.

The file description can be edited by pressing Shift+F2.

.topic IgnoreSelection
The Ignore selection command (Alt+I) toggles the mode in which
file operations are always performed only on the file (directory)
on which the cursor is located, even if there are marked files in the panel
(catalogs). In this case, the bottom line of the panel displays information
about this file (directory).
