.topic DriveListDlg
The Drive list dialog box contains a list of all available drives.
with basic information for each of them: logical name, volume label,
classification, cluster size, total volume and free disk space.

When the Open Drive list flag is enabled, instead of Drive letter
The Drive list dialog box will always open instead of the window
{Drive letter:DriveDialog}, for example, when pressing the keys
Alt+F1 and Alt+F2 in the {File Manager:Panel} window.

When the Get drives from User defined drive list flag is enabled
all windows designed for displaying and selecting logical drives,
will always show only those disks that were included in
dialog box {User defined drive list:UserDefinedDriveList},
called when you click the User defined drive list button.

The Enable User defined network resources flag allows the use of
own list of network resources. Window {Redirected devices:RedirList},
appears when you press the [\] button in a dialog box
{Drive letter:DriveDialog}, as well as the window panel {File Manager:Panel}
in the mode of displaying a list of logical drives and network resources
will show only those resources that were included in
dialog box {User defined network resources:UserDefinedNetList},
called when the User defined resources button is clicked.

When you execute the Select command, the selected disk becomes the current disk.

When you run the Reread command, the disk list is recreated.
If you hold down the Ctrl or Shift keys, the program
will access floppy disk drives to obtain information
about the volume label, file system and disk sizes, otherwise
This information will not be displayed for floppy disks.

The Volume label and S/N commands are used to edit the disk label.
(up to 32 characters for the NTFS file system) and a serial number.
The disk label can only be changed
{when running under Windows NT:CN_NT}, and the serial number - only under
DOS (Windows 9x) Long disk label is now displayed on
dividing line in the Info panel of the {File Manager:Panel} window.

.topic UserDefinedDriveList
The User defined drive list dialog box is designed to create
own list of logical drives in case of automatic
determining the system disks and their types for various reasons
undesirable (DOS functions called in this case may lead to
system errors or slow down the program). The window contains
list of Drives (A:..Z:), list of possible Disk classes
and buttons Auto-detect disks, Enable/Disable, Change class,
and also the Toggle LFN flag button (Gray Plus hotkey),
allows you to disable support for the Win95 LFN API for the current element
in the Drives list.

To include a drive in the User defined drive list, it is enough
place the cursor on it in the list of disks and double-click
"mouse" by the corresponding type in the Disk classes list.

.topic UserDefinedNetList
The User defined network resources dialog box is designed to create
own list of network resources. The window contains the generated
the user's list of Network resources and the Auto-detect button,
Modify, New, Delete, Enable/Disable, Move up/down (hotkeys)
Ctrl+Up/Ctrl+Down), as well as the Toggle LFN flag button (hotkey
Gray Plus), which allows you to disable support for the Win95 LFN API for
the current item in the Network resources list.

.topicNewNetListItem
Enter the new network resource name in UNC format:

\\<servername>\<sharename>

If the Resource enabled flag is not enabled, the resource will not be
appear in the list of {network resources:RedirList}.

If the Win95 LFN API enabled flag is not enabled, the resource
Win95 LFN API support will not be provided.

Redirected device.

.topic IncrSearch,ArcIncrSearch
Press the keys corresponding to the letters of the file name in sequence
(lowercase letters) or directory (uppercase letters). To search for the next

.topic DataViewer
{ dBASE view window :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The window for viewing .DBF files contains the contents of the records of the selected
databases (fields are separated by vertical lines). Navigate through the database
data can be accessed using the mouse or keyboard.

The indicator in the lower left corner of the window shows the absolute and relative
(%) is the number of the record where the cursor is located.

The dBASE viewer window menu is called by right-clicking or by pressing
Alt+F10 keys.

You can move, resize, and close the window using
{Window} menu item commands.

To add a new record to the end of the database file, press the Enter key.
(Ctrl+Enter) or double-click the mouse button. In this case, at the cursor position
a new empty line will appear (if Ctrl+Enter keys were pressed, the line
will be filled with the contents of the current record). In order to insert a new
To record at the cursor position, press Shift+Enter (or Ctrl+Shift+Enter).
To change the contents of the fields of a previously entered entry, press Alt+Enter
(if this key combination is reserved by the system for other purposes,
you can press Alt+J or Ctrl+Space).

The following commands are possible in edit or input mode:

Right: Cursor to the right
Left: Cursor to the left
End: Cursor to the end of the field
Home: Cursor to the beginning of the field
Ctrl+End: Cursor to the end of the entry
Ctrl+Home: Move cursor to the beginning of the entry
Tab,
Ctrl+Right: Cursor to the next field
Shift+Tab,
Ctrl+Left: Move cursor to the previous field
Ins: Mode Switching
<insert/replace symbol>
Del: Delete the character at the cursor position
BackSpace: Delete the character before the cursor
Ctrl+Y: Fill the field with spaces
Ctrl+Z: Fill the entry with spaces

The cursor can also be moved using the mouse by pressing its left button.

After finishing editing or after entering all fields, press the key
Enter or double-click the mouse button. To cancel the input or
Press the Esc key to edit.

Database entries can be marked with the '*' symbol as deleted by clicking
on the Del key. In order to restore the entry (unmark),
Press Ctrl+Del.

Records in the database window can be selected for group operations
{Delete records:DeleteRecord} and {Export to text:ExportData} by clicking
using the Ins, Space, Shift+arrow keys, and also using the mouse.
To select all records, press Ctrl+A (Select all).
Deselect - Gray Minus key.

Pressing Ctrl+@ activates the sequential search mode.
by letters ({Incremental search:EditIncSearch}).

.topic DataFields
This window lists all fields of the selected database.
and their characteristics. If the database is empty, the Edit command calls
the {New database:DBCreate} dialog box, where you can add,
change and delete fields.

.topic ViewMemo
The View memo (View memo as Hex) command in the {dBASE view window:DataViewer} window
opens {Text view window:TextViewer} ({Hex view window:HexViewer})
with comments on the current entry, if any.

.topic DeleteRecord
The Delete records command in the {dBASE view window:DataViewer} window deletes
after confirmation, the current record or all selected records from
the database file being viewed. The operation can be quite
long if the database is large and the records are located at the beginning of the file.

.topic PackDataBase
The Pack database command in the {dBASE view window:DataViewer} window removes
After confirmation, all records marked with '*' from the viewed
database file.

See also {Delete record:DeleteRecord}

.topic ZapDataBase
The Zap database command in the {dBASE view window:DataViewer} window after
confirmation clears all records in the viewed database file,
making it empty.
{ATTENTION!!!:Color_4}
This command results in the loss of {ALL:Color_2} information,
stored in the database.

.topic FieldCursor
The Field cursor on/off command toggles the mode of the cursor that selects
the current record or field when viewing the contents of a window
{dBASE view window:DataViewer}.

The Clear In XLAT table (?) and Clear Out XLAT table (?) commands cancel

current window {dBASE view window:DataViewer}.

See also {Set XLAT files:DBXLATFile}

.topic DBConvertDates
The Convert date fields command switches the mode in which the window
{dBASE view window:DataViewer} Date type fields are displayed in the format,
determined by the settings of the {Country settings:OCountry} dialog.

.topic DBValidate
The Validate numeric fields command toggles the mode in which the window
{dBASE view window:DataViewer} when editing numeric fields and
fields of the Date type of the current record do not allow entering invalid characters,
and before saving the edited entry to the file or when
{import data:ImportData} the correctness of the contents of such is checked
fields.

.topic ImportData
The Import from text command (Alt+I) adds records to the database
from the selected text file. The lines of the text file should
contain the text of the database fields, terminated by the symbol
{field separator:FieldSeparator}, for example:

Field1:Field2:Field3:Field4

It is allowed to place one entry on several lines, for example:

LongField1:LongField2:LongField3
LongField4:LongField5:LongField6

as well as multiple entries in one line, for example:

Field1:Field2 : Field1:Field2

If a record is to have a deletion flag, the text string must
start with the '*' character.

See also {Export to text:ExportData}

.topic ExportData
The Export to text command (Alt+V) creates a text file containing
database records in which the text of each field ends with the character
{field separator:FieldSeparator}.

See also {Import from text:ImportData}

.topic ImpExpOptions
The Import/Export options command allows you to set the options used when
operations {Import from text:ImportData} and {Export to text:ExportData}.

The Data Import options radio buttons allow you to choose how to place the data.
imported records into the database file: append to the end of the file
(Add records to the end of the database) or insert before record,
where the cursor is located (Insert records at the cursor position).
If the second method is selected, then before inserting each record, the data in
the file has to be moved, which in the case of a large database and
a small index of the current record can significantly slow down the execution
operations.

The Numeric fields right-justified flag specifies that when importing data
The text in the numeric fields of the records being created must be aligned
to the right edge.

The Trim leading whitespaces flag specifies that when exporting data,
remove spaces from the left of the field text.

The Trim trailing whitespaces flag specifies that when exporting data,
remove spaces to the right of the field text.

.topic FieldSeparator
The Field separator command allows you to specify the field separator character,
used in the operations {Import from text:ImportData} and
{Export to text:ExportData}.

.topic SortDatabase
The Sort database command allows you to sort records in a database file.
by the selected field. The Sort direction radio buttons allow you to specify
sorting direction (ascending, descending -
Descending). The Case sensitive flag allows comparison of string fields.
case-sensitive or case-insensitive. The Filter deleted flag allows
place records marked as deleted separately at the end of the database
(Ascending) or at the beginning (Descending). In the Field position input line
You can specify from which position to compare string or numeric fields.
{ATTENTION!!!:Color_4}
Sorting records in a database changes the order in which the data is stored.
in a file on disk.

.topic HTMLViewer
{ HTML view window :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
HTML viewer is designed to view files created in the format
HTML (Hypertext Markup Language). You can navigate the file with
using the mouse or keyboard:

Up Move up one line
Down Go down a line
Right Shift one character to the right
Left Shift one character to the left

PgDn Scroll down one page

Ctrl+PgDn Move to the end of the file

Ctrl+Right Move one word to the right
Ctrl+Home Move to the top line
Ctrl+End Move to the bottom line

The indicator in the lower left corner of the window shows the current position of the cursor,
and also the block selection mode: solid [] or vertical [].
The '' symbol means that the cursor is on a hypertext link.

You can move, resize, and close the window using
{Window} menu item commands.

The HTML viewer window menu is called by right-clicking.
or by pressing Alt+F10.

HTML viewer window commands:

Ctrl+U Command {Search again:SHSearchAgain} (repeat search for a string, Forward)
Ctrl+V Command {Reload:HTMLReload}
Ctrl+W Opens the HTMLHistory window.
Ctrl+@ Incremental search mode ({Incremental search:EditIncSearch})
Space Selects the word at the cursor position for the {Search again:SHSearchAgain} command
Ctrl+\ Go to the {File Manager:Panel} window and search for the current file

.topic RegExpDlg
The Regular expression debugger dialog box is designed for debugging.
{regular expressions:RegExp}. For example, if in the top three lines
enter text:

Source { One song (track01).mp3 :AbsColor_$1f}
Search { (.*)( )(\(track..\))(.mp3) :AbsColor_$1f}
Replace { \2\1\0\3 :AbsColor_$1f}

then the result will be displayed in the lower lines:

Result { (track01) One song.mp3 :AbsColor_$1f}
Group 0 { One song :AbsColor_$1f}
Group 1 { ﾛ :AbsColor_$1f}
Group 2 { (track01) :AbsColor_$1f}
Group 3 { .mp3 :AbsColor_$1f}

When you click the OK button, the following actions are performed automatically:

if the current program window is the {File Manager:Panel} window,
the {Rename/Move:RenMovDialog} dialog box will open (while holding down
Shift key - dialog box {Copy:CopyDialog}) with the destination string,
formed from the Search and Replace strings:

{>(.*)( )(\(track..\))(.mp3)>\2\1\0\3:Color_2}

if the current program window is the {text editor:ASCIIEditor} window,
The {Replace} dialog box will open (while holding down the Shift key -
{Find} dialog box) with the Search and Replace strings and the flag enabled
Regular expression.

.topic CN_NT
{Working under Windows NT :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
When working in a DOS window of the Windows NT operating system (Windows 2000,
(Windows XP and others) the program provides the following features:

  Full Windows NT Clipboard support
  Correct definition sizes disks ( in volume including NTFS)
  Correct definition list logical disks And type disks
  { Sizes :DirSizes} of compressed (Compressed) files (Size on disk)
  { Launch others applications And associations :NT_Exec} without restrictions lengths
command line with the ability to redirect output to a file
  { Deleting :NT_Recycle} files And catalogs V basket
  { Information O system :SInfo}, extended information O processor
  Reading And installation long tags disk V dialogic window {Drive list:DriveListDlg}
  Support work With title DOS - windows (Application Title)
  Exit from programs at closing windows or at the end sessions
  Reading And installation times creation And last access To files ,
as well as special {file attributes:FileAttributes} (Compressed and Encrypted)
  { Copying files :NT_SysCopy} with using Windows API functions CopyFileEx()
  Automatic rereading panels windows {File Manager:Panel}
when changes are made to directories

.topic NT_Recycle
The dialog box that asks you to confirm the deletion of files and directories contains
Recycle switch, which can be turned on {when running under Windows NT:CN_NT}
Allows you to delete to the trash.

.topic NT_SysCopy
In dialog boxes related to copying and moving files
and directories ({Copy:CopyDialog}, {Shift+Copy:ShiftCopyDialog},
{Rename / Move:RenMovDialog}, {Shift+Rename / Move:ShiftRenMovDialog}),
There is a SysCopy switch, which can be turned on
{when running under Windows NT:CN_NT} allows you to copy files
using the Windows API function CopyFileEx(), which may be faster
(but in some cases not) than regular copying.

.topic NT_Exec
{ Running programs under Windows NT :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
{When running under Windows NT:CN_NT} directive {$XNT:Directives}(Flags, Option)
allows you to run programs using the operating system itself.
The Flags parameter specifies the flags used when calling the function.
Windows API CreateProcess:

create_Suspended = $00000004;
detached_Process = $00000008;
create_New_Console = $00000010;
normal_Priority_Class = $00000020;
idle_Priority_Class = $00000040;
high_Priority_Class = $00000080;
realtime_Priority_Class = $00000100;
create_New_Process_Group = $00000200;
create_Unicode_Environment = $00000400;
create_Separate_Wow_Vdm = $00000800;
create_Share_Wow_Vdm = $00001000;
create_Default_Error_Mode = $04000000;
create_No_Window = $08000000;

The Option parameter determines the startup mode.

eoErrIgnore = 1 Ignore startup errors
eoErrZero = 2 Always return 0 (successful launch)
eoAsync = 4 Asynchronous (without waiting for completion) launch

The special Flags and Option values (-1, -1) and (1, 1) allow you to run
programs (and other files) as if they were run from the shell
Windows using Windows Associations. Values (-1, -1) allow
run in normal, and (1, 1) - in the maximum opened window.

The $XNT directive must be used in conjunction with the
{$CMD:Directives}, however, in this case the cmd file is not created,
and the command line expanded in the buffer is passed to the ExecNT function. For example:

Program path: $REPORT $XNT(0, 3)
Command line:
PIC\bin\picc.exe -E -O -G -Zg -INTEL -D24 -ASMLIST
-M$lPATH$lNAME.map -$PROMPT(16F73 -DB400 -RESROMFFA-FFF -L-Pid=ffah)
$lPATH$lNAME$lEXT $cmd

runs the same picc compiler as in the example for the directive
{$CMD:Directives}, with the same output redirection, but without
using additional programs, only by means of Windows NT.

The next design

Program path: "$LPATH$LNAME$LEXT" $XNT(1, 1)
Command line:

will launch Windows Associations for the corresponding file in the maximum
in the extended window. For the specified value of options and flags, the $CMD directive
not used.

The $XNT directive can be used in the settings of archivers under Windows.
For example, for zip:

Packer name $REPORT $XNT(0, 3)
Unpacker name $REPORT $XNT(0, 3)
Extract PKZIP25.EXE -extract -overwrite $ARC $SRC $CMD
...

This mechanism allows you to work with long file names and paths.
without the problem of them not fitting into 128 bytes
DOS command line.

.topic TopicSearch

  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ

.topic LITERAL
" Literal.

The following characters can be used in strings:

\a 0x07 BEL Beep
\b 0x08 BS Slaughter
\f 0x0C FF Translation of the form
\n 0x0A LF New line
(line break)
\r 0x0D CR Carriage return
\t 0x09 HT Horizontal tab
\v 0x0B VT Vertical tab
\\ 0x5c \ Backslash
\O any O = string up to three
octal digits
\xH any H = string
hexadecimal digits
\XH any H = string
hexadecimal digits

S = "string", {PRINTS}("hello", 1)

Note: When using string constants containing
full file names, the '\' characters must be doubled, for example:

C:\\AUTOEXEC.BAT

.topic POINTER
&(): Ptr

A pointer to a Common function. The function has the following calling format:

Func(var E, D, C, B, A : Longint) : Longint;
al = function number from the following list:

Stop GetData GetCommon Init_RS
Menu Send CheckRS Receive
SendBlock ReceiveBlk GetBuff ReadBuff
WriteBuff KeyPrs FOpen FClose
RdBlk WrBlk PrintS InputS
PrintV InputV RTS CTS
DTR DSR IndBar NotL
DispBuff User LoadUser CRC32
Beep Idle

If al >= 80H:

Func(Var A, B : Longint) : Longint;
al - 80H = function number from the following list:

MulL DivL AddL SubL AndL XorL OrL
LE GE NE EQ LS GR Let
Empty

Pointers to parameters are pushed onto the stack at the specified
order. The function result is returned in registers
DX:AX. The function DOES NOT release the parameters from the stack.
(C - calling agreement).

.topic BRACKETS
()

Brackets.

A = ((A+B)*C+D)/(A*3+2+5*(EF/2))

will be carried out in accordance with the rules of mathematics.

.topic MUL
*

Operation. Multiplies the left operand by the right one.

D = A * B
E = C * 5
F = 2 * 3

.topic PLUS
+

Operation. Adds the left and right operands.

A + B, C + 5, 2 + 3.

.topic MINUS
-

Operation. Subtracts the right operand from the left one.

A - B, C - 5, 2 - 3.

-

Unary minus.

B = -A, C = -5.

.topic DIV
/

Operation. Integer divides the left operand by
right.

D = A / B
E = C / 5
F = 2 / 3 rem 2 / 3 = 0 !.

.topic SEMICLN
;

Operation: Treats one string as two or more.

GETBUF(B, 100); GETBUF(D, 1000); I = 0 ; GOTO L1

When using ';', expressions separated by ';' are executed
in the order they are written. The given line is equivalent
the following sequence:

GETBUF(B, 100)
GETBUF(D, 1000)
I = 0
GOTO L1

.topic LESS
<

Operation: Less than between left and right operands.

(A < B)

.topic LE
<=

Operation: Less than equal between left and right
operands.

(A <= B)

.topic NE
<>

Operation: Not equal between left and right operands.

(A <> B)

.topic E
=

Operation. Assigns a value to the left operand.
right.

A = D = B + C

.topic EE
==

Operation: Equal to left and right operands.

(A == B)

.topic GREATER
>

Operation. Greater than between left and right operands.

(A > B)

.topic GE
>=

Operation: Greater than equal between left and right
operands.

(A >= B)

.topic ADDRESS
@(): Ptr

A pointer to the program data segment. The data segment contains
variables used in the program, in the order they appear in the text.
Each variable takes 4 bytes.

.topic AND
AND

Operation. Performs a logical (bitwise) "AND" between
left and right operands.

(A > B) AND (B < C)

.topic BEEP
BEEP(F: Int, T: Int)

Procedure: Generates an audio signal with a frequency of F Hz and a duration of T ms.

BEEP(440, 100)

.topic CMPSTR
CMPSTR(S1, S2 : Str [, C : Bool]) : Code

Function. Compares strings S1 and S2. Returns 1 if S1 is greater than S2;
2 if S2 is greater than S1; 0 if the strings are the same. When C <> 0, the register
doesn't matter.

.topic IDLE

any cycle of the user program. When F <> 0 does not allow
the {Terminal} window to intercept characters coming through the serial port.

IDLE()

.topic INDBAR
INDBAR(I : Bool, M : LInt [, D : Bool]) [: LInt]

Procedure. When I = True, it displays on the screen, and when I = False, it closes
window with a "slider". M is the size of the transmitted buffer. If D = True,
The slider moves from right to left. If there's already a window with a slider on the screen,
The procedure increments its internal counter and redraws it.

.topic INITRS
INITRS(S:Str):Code

Function: Initializes the serial port.
S is a parameter string. If S = "", then the port
initialized with default parameters,
installed by the {Communication:OMode} command
Options menu item. The options line looks like this:

"COM2,9600,8,2,N[,Port,Irq,Vect,HWFlow,SWFlow]"

Programming the COM2 serial port on
9600 baud rate, 8-bit word length, two stop bits
and without parity control.

The optional parameters HWFlow and SWFlow are calculated as the sum
the following constants:

Hardware flow control
$01 Use DTR
$02 Use RTS
$04 Require DSR
$08 Require CTS
$10 DTR active low
$20 RTS active low
$40 DSR active low
$80 CTS active low

Software flow control
$01 Receiver flow
$02 Transmitter flow

If S = "T", the program opens the {Terminal} window, after which the functions
data input/output ({SEND}, {SNDBLK}, {RECEIV}, {RECBLK}) work through
serial port of this window, and the display functions ({PRINTS}, {PRINTV})
use this window instead of the {Output:OutputWindow} window (except in the case where
when the last parameter passed to these functions is not equal to 0).

.topic RDBUF
RDBUF(B : Ptr, I : Word [, C : Byte]) : LInt

Function. If C = 0 or 1, reads the 1-th (starting from zero) byte from
array B. When C = 2 or 4, reads C bytes from array B, starting from the 1st.

V = RDBUF(B, 5) reads the 5th byte of array B.
Tick = RDBUF($0040006C, 0, 4) reads the time from
BIOS Data Area.

See also

{GETBUF}
{WRBUF}

.topic RECBLK
RECBLK(B : Ptr, N : Word [, T : Word] [, I : Bool] [, P : Word]) : Code

Function. Accepts N bytes per block. If T <> 0, waits T sec. If I <> 0,
Doesn't move the slider. Accepts the result code value:
0 - success, 0th bit - Esc, 1st - buffer overflow, 2nd - error,
3rd - timeout. P - port number.

C = RECBLK(B,128)

See also

{DISBUF}
{WRBUF}
{RDBUF}

{RDBLK}
{SNDBLK}

0 - success, 0th bit - Esc, 1st - buffer overflow, 2nd - error,

UPLOAD([S : Str], [N : Word], [P : Word])

.topic PUSER
USER(U : Ptr, B, C) [: LInt]

Function. Launches the program loaded using {LODUSR}
or a program linked using {?Lfname?:Link},
in this case, if B and C are arrays, in registers
transmitted:

BX = length C CX = length B
ES = Segment C DS = Segment B
DI = Offset C SI = Offset B

If B or C are not arrays, the following is passed in registers:

CX = 0 BX = 0
ES = C high byte DS = B high byte
DI = low byte of C SI = low byte of B

Takes the value AX + 10000H * DX.

The program must begin with the line:

Db 14,'Connect_User_1' ,

do not change the SS, SP, BP registers and end with a far return RETF.
Using any input/output operations in a program may result in
to unpredictable consequences. If B and C are arrays, then the program will not
must change registers ES, DI, DS, SI.

.topic WAIT
WAIT(S : String, T : Word, [F : Bool], [P : Word]) : Bool

Function. Waits for the sequence specified in line S to arrive within
T seconds. Case is not important. Returns True if it waited.
False - if the time has expired. When waiting, it works similarly to the {IDLE} procedure.
When F <> 0, the buffer in which the incoming data was accumulated is not cleared.
the sequence of bytes from the previous call to this function.
P - port number.

R = WAIT("LOGIN", 10)

.topic WRBUF

.topic ConnectLang
{ CONNECT Language :AbsColor_$5F} ﾜ
  ﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟﾟ
The built-in programming language is designed to describe protocols
exchange via a serial port with remote systems, as well as
for writing programs to control a text editor.

The following data types are supported: long integer (4 bytes),
pointer to buffer and pointer to string.

Variables can have arbitrary names consisting of the following
symbols: 0..9, _, $, A..Z, a..z; case does not matter.

Constants can consist of numbers or start with the $ symbol.
In the latter case, the number is perceived as hexadecimal. If
the compiler did not perceive the operand as a constant, it perceives it as
as a variable name. String constants must be enclosed in
{" ":LITERAL}.

All variables are global.

Labels can have arbitrary names.

Operations {/:DIV}, {*:MUL}, {-:MINUS}, {+:PLUS}, {AND}, {OR}, {XOR},
{<=:LE}, {>=:GE}, {<>:NE}, {==:EE}, {<:LESS}, {>:GREATER}, {=:E}, {|:STICK}
are performed in the specified sequence, which can be changed
using brackets {():BRACKETS}.

The language has a sufficient set of {built-in functions:TopicSearch}, but can
be extended by using the {USER:PUSER} function.

A minimal set of control structures is supported:

{IF}, {GOSUB}, {GOTO}, {RET}.

The language allows you to perform operations on string variables:

{CMPSTR}, {CONCAT}, {COPY}, {DELETE},
{FMTSTR}, {INSERT}, {LOCASE}, {POS},
{UPCASE}.

All program debugging modes are supported. The debugged program can be
compiled into a file and run using {Load icon:ULoadIcon}.

.topic CompilerError
Internal error. Please report it to the developers.

.topic CEOutOfMemory
Low memory. Too many large buffers, or too many
open windows, or too many loaded programs.

.topic CEProgramTooLarge
The program is too big.

.topic CEQuoteExpected
Missing {quote marks:Literal}.

.topic CECollectionError
Error creating list of tags.

.topic CESyntaxError
Syntax error. See {Keywords:TopicSearch}.

.topic CEInvalidBracks
{parentheses:Brackets} are incorrectly specified.

.topic CEBrackExpected,CEBrackExpected1,CEBrackExpected2
Missing {parenthesis:Brackets}.

.topic CEInvalidLabel
The label is incorrect.

.topic CEErrorInExpression
Error in expression.

.topic CEDuplicateLabels
Duplicate tags.

.topic CEInvalidLabPos
The label is in the wrong place.

.topic CEInvalidIFPos
The {IF} statement is incorrectly specified.

.topic CEErrorInIFTHEN
Error in using {IF...THEN:IF} operators.

.topic CELabelExpected
The label is missing.

.topic CEWriteFileError
Error writing to listing file.

.topic CECouldNotCreateOutput
Error creating listing file.

.topic CEUnknownLabel
Label not defined.

.topic CEInvalidGOTOAddress
The {GOTO} label specified is invalid.

.topic CEFileNotFound
No file with the given name was found. The path may not have been specified.

.topic CEFigBrackExpected
Missing {curly brace:Link}.

.topic CEErrorInInteger
Invalid integer constant specified.

.topic Error
Internal error. Please report it to the developers.

.topic ProgramNotFound
The program file (file with extension .CBB) was not found.

.topic InvalidProgram
Invalid program file structure (file with .CBB extension).

.topic SourceNotFound
The source file (file with extension .CBS) was not found.

.topic MemAllocError
Error allocating memory block.

.topicInvalidPtrOperation
Invalid operation on buffer or string.

.topic InvalidRSInitLine
The RS-232 initialization parameters are not set correctly. See {INITRS}.

.topic StackOverflow
Return stack overflow. Too many nested subroutines.
Probably a looping subroutine call.

.topic RETWithoutGOSUB
The {RET} operator without a preceding {GOSUB} operator.

.topic FileNotClosed
Attempting to reopen an open file.

.topic CouldNotOpenFile
Error opening file. Invalid path specified,
low disk space, etc.

.topic UserFileNotFound,UserFileNotFound1,UserFileNotFound2
USER file not found or USER file header does not start
with DB 14,'Connect_User_1'.

.topic DivisionByZero,DivisionByZero1,DivisionByZero2,DivisionByZero3
Division by zero.

.topic NoEditor
When executing procedures or functions that control a text editor
It is necessary that at least one {editor window:ASCIIEditor} (not counting
window with the program being debugged) was opened.
To open the editor window from your program, use the function
{NewWin}.

.topicInvalidBufferIndex
Invalid index value when accessing a buffer (array).

.topic OutOfMemory,OutOfMemory1
Low memory. Too many large buffers, or too many
open windows, or too many loaded programs.

.topicInvalidPtrOperation1
Invalid operation on buffer or string.

.topic IndexOutOfRange
The index when accessing the array (buffer) exceeds 64000.

.topic ValueOutOfRange
The value exceeds the acceptable range.

.topic InvalidNumFormat,InvalidNumFormat1
Invalid format when entering a number.

.topic DiskError
Error during file and disk operations.
Invalid path specified, low disk space, etc.

.topic FileNotOpen
Attempting to perform file operations without first opening the file.
See {OPEN}.

.topicInvalidUserFile
The USER file header does not start with DB 14,'Connect_User_1'.

.topic UserFileTooLarge
USER file is larger than 64000 bytes.

.topic ErrorStop
Execute the {STOP} statement or press Esc in the file dialog.

.topic InternalOverflow,InternalOverflow1,InternalOverflow2
Return stack overflow. Too many nested subroutines.
Probably a looping subroutine call.

.topic UserBreak
Ctrl+Break keys pressed.

.topic PortNotInitialized
Attempt to use functions {SEND}, {SNDBLK}, {RECEIV}, {RECBLK},
{UPLOAD:UPLD}, {DNLOAD} without executing the {INITRS} function.
